eMarketer Ups Programmatic

 

Programmatic buying continues its upward trend, with eMarketer revising its estimate from $3.34 billion in RTB spending in 2013 to $3.37 billion. MAGNA GLOBAL expects $3.9 billion in RTB ad spending this year, the highest of all firms eMarketer measured. Improvements in quality and adoption among publishers as well as buyers has led to huge gains for programmatic. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOh7vxXx2MOH3e-zyKqHKtlPe3p9aUUTPCL7kMEocca2d1C3ohuAa4sIPOE97Exz7Uz9y7qrQ-MTnQ0IGOph1Te9O1w5wfBI7xtf0y-by3ZwHwt5Ure1CnlM3NYCm9LnFd2eMcssLn5UdXTraMzRrOFAT7cXTOz_yVkheio3K_Dl_fgFAlDMGT-jEID3MVATnfsoc-HAlnJ4zpQBihrzSEtV> .

 

FB Ads

 

Adweek offers a short burst on whether Facebook is putting too many ads on its site. A 66% increase in revenue for FB is one side of the story. An anonymous agency exec offers another side: "[Teens are] interested in what friends are sharing. They're not interested in what brands are sharing." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOhlyn3kVvTpckw65t-FUh9gjIAf53Fba28wn3TpE__83egVJ4-r1gHciizk1BP_z5Hg7tlpulumD0CtJ2uGJjxhrCHfpzpdlhhZdxOkTHtCkzw3_r5l_yIU3353kH-0_nrGVBRjByDkivrQ_18NkdLpKvV9cuXCOza_3XvzcKAW_VYLX48ndvvQ0hJOJVJtt1A=> . But on GigaOm, advertisers appreciate Facebook's "walled garden" and lack of advertising fraud compared to other inventory sources. Read more from Jeff John Roberts <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOjtB42a6p774P0L7at1aKnTXNIVnXWoSJB4yc9fMC9BTNBm76ITLa-vUmk0G4Jz1BO3vzWy5pR76YAJv8DhUZEmXqGX8SQRF6fZ-_9HFvNA9AZnt_e74z9xloiodaUJBhaQncp7gz_ftcUwN3KV4wAGeHQtZZdQfFVVA4tU2XZ48nEskgpybBbSn0kLaTMwD4sQ0krYvrjsL0TrfgDBfsekKCADr9zSFLiwL5fSJkYraw==> .

 

The New News

 

Led by CEO Jonah Peretti (who will appear at Industry Preview 2014 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOh9SZrQY27o-MugMkfY1sqjSmexoSVQSfsTMmvpqmIL1nv49sZ3v6EqYb1450mXKvDnRAlZIAzRtnomgQANDiPMcGHyZogMDJRLoIIh0SgPxQrFoLNgvQt2> ), BuzzFeed is navigating the stormy publisher seas trying to create a new business model that has some singing its praises, and leaving others with a bad taste. The Independent provides a featurey look as the company blurs, or reimagines, the lines between advertiser and publisher, making sponsored content almost indistinguishable from regular content. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOh5Y9mFxIrUD3sl6Tst0H2gYSwoJ9yp7-GwEutqEQiqk9vNNtfJ4whEV_YgU9eiV6qy_iBiyRvXrTV7y39BY__8zMlGmwpGoQV7RidoFXtyX5CuPbys812gFdkNMZU7m41VG-XwzKqo8OJLI0B16nBrNoXBkPujZcYl6xqVO_3wNDOFHGBlo4e_YQHswsaCq340ioJ2J7pAi-xaDvLyprF4w_3uXlWOV_GW0dGVUCRelnPPOZTogE0TvJfJEiLSg2s=> .

 

Man Vs. Machine

 

PrecisionDemand set out to prove that machine buys are smarter than human buys, and according to its results, that may be true. Ad Age published some of the numbers, including a campaign that had 4,000 more subscribers than a previous one that used traditional buying methods. According to the report, "The amount of viewing behavior increases 800 fold from 25,000 to 20 million persons." This opens up more inventory to advertisers and better matches people to shows they may not have thought to watch before. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOjqhj1Eya_lufEqwuDtzms80XUWX6ZqSloy_gnl4BEZc0-V3iXAAxqhst1WvPOw8f_FUsRJ9IxOvIlhkmwkCd6kFxOK1EiIJa9PokhydwvZ3A9fP8bu3b3YIeXNckJ2zEMzq3UWXu4Bggg28cIpxv1_N1j4tlHmnI5jgkvhx9XA0JXWh_fhjqLNcwRacI36SahVLZ29w5ImVQ==> .

 

Creative Data

 

Data and creativity will work together in advertising, says Neustar exec Paul McLenaghan. He writes on iMedia Connection, "Think of it as creativity enabled by science." Creativity is empowered by transparency and efficiency, not lost because of it. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOi1gYT-eTcDNw1yNf_K3nCIplKXGqP9aniAWH4tPdW492ZptW_-PfAIiry3i2kv32Sj97rtPOM6KAa8nFWx7oE-ZASr37zQUe3BhhoKDx1eTdOQGrME-QjvI1-_ltBc5KEU7kUE9rQlf3qnR8kUaoGexlBmWXz25tYyA3UH9gEtmvwug_GhiMDmvZarpZCBMCq7lcYtX2lVdw==> . A mantra that many creative agencies need to embrace.

TV Is Dying

 

On Business Insider, Jim Edwards cobbles together a group of nice charts and data that he says shows the "cord is being cut" and traditional television is dying. A ratings decline is one indicator, says Edwards, who adds, "We're at the beginning of a major historical shift from watching TV to watching video -- including TV shows and movies -- on the Internet or on mobile devices. ... Nearly 5 million cable TV subscribers have gone elsewhere in the last five years. The number of cable TV-only subscribers remaining could sink below 40 million later this year, according to this data from ISI Group, an equity research firm." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOg_yGgLxlJ8zEN3pwVTcmGttXNXkwSqW8btaXhd9KtnDYqsEdyxCBafcFQ9o7wM-TNcAm5NmPzM3yWdGKEkGmFInLYvNADii2OGl0s4tBvSISvIdm9hj0vdgta5xZoeYyxHXZ806W3H7E3v9bgO8o4hjQJPfVVlxQOtducMjYJcnw==> .

 

Photo Lift

 

Instagram ads are new, but on the surface they seem to be working. According to Digiday and analytics firm Nitrogram, Michael Kors experienced a 370% increase in followers, and other brands such as Lexus have seen similar positive results. What's next for Instagram is figuring out ROI for brands and better targeting options. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FuxOmkXOhOhSke09qqX-jKlQqS0FnmM8aA27JxI0UUjJTTndzLyn9ry0pXzVSaLd1mNHf6Pwn9xJPmg3WRfmpsA1aRHV4a4Vbk3bLLKTHZcMV0M_poEvPloBM-BMfryy6lK2h4kJHuyN9ZMQ0AocBuzP96uc4SnCvLbfPMbcVHK7F3XP6KmZVlsZHVSH915i> .

Email Fandom

 

In reviewing rock bands' email marketing efforts, The Wall Street Journal's Hannah Karp says new data from ecommerce music website manager Topspin shows email is the gift that keeps on giving. Karp notes the power of growing fan base loyalty: "Fans who get free music in exchange for an email address are 11 times more likely to make future purchases directly from a band than fans who get nothing for forking over their contact details." Read it (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xDTkpRcuPrbaUCdSscdXq_wHAlRminU7spa8wrFjOCBFvaHB5hpJlW8ScN_a0tFGMTikC_VNlK-HT9Tw6HLYttMszStPm8duNcwuvFajrqqrhj3FF6GNj2PAP52ObkMza8R8B1etVWRtzcHqeJ55SUMVIH8KU9hyyILCBPqD1RjZz8mCwI8rRHxpF8zin782lqxkYtgbwy4=> .

 

End Of Trolls

 

Former DoubleClick-er Kevin O'Connor said "no" to patent trolls dogging his company, FindTheBest, and appears to have won -- at least in the short term. According to Ars Technica, the patent trolling firm was trying to patent "matchmaking" and US District Court Judge Denise Cote was having none of it, writing in her court order: "There is no inventive idea here. Having two or more parties input preference data is not inventive. Matchmakers have been doing this for millennia. ... It is merely a mathematical manifestation of the underlying process behind matchmaking: determining good matches." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xDTkpRcuPrZDsbbhK-5FvEwr-zAa9uSs_pYGIb__8-LK-bHgIXWxyEt82jxiCZHvxE7HEZh8mHg5QROUSo06_h0fEHGgcdGzvHq-cOBds8Mna7VUkgqfRCMLSwql022Sok6vAQ--eiOvIgMCv69mYO8WfeUx-b6EAVDLRAEprSDWJHmkswoSAXjpyZskS7fndKb5QhCM9usmAO753CP1wvdPXOtlSkNv9bH4xHH21d5YTDTkGxQWfRONW83TnrE3> . The only downside thus far is the $200,000 in court fees vs. $50,000 the patent troll wanted in order to settle. Also, read AdExchanger's 2012 interview <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xDTkpRcuPrZM2A6Lj853T8iteZzDK1GrK4vvgvzBEkjvsWLAMOJaA8sArzvYJnVsOguzLnWc6PdkDzTH1xNEhPvDwApGmTwk16NHCL1kxihZDDgO4YIk5DHCMh8G4dqWnABAcem1VyhxgnM59QbZfOoILlYU2hBzx_sWtz_rsh8=>  with O'Connor.

 

Geofencing Ads

 

On his Screenwerk blog, analyst Greg Sterling reviews ads that use Placecast data through Harman's Aha Radio app. Targeting involves geofencing and sandwich shop Quiznos is the first advertiser, reports Sterling. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xDTkpRcuPrYwt3nUckzEkdfe9DbveklKb75g5nL0PSibuvKJa8UoEpbHT9dNxZVves-NbLWRfy2dpQr0RjqLQeUFj-1ry1AJzyYP70CXrndBH44yRnkXdBnph9_vbKJ3X9wwcDRXIOZli49-InGJEwxjS_9gHVPp7P-ek5A9tTpH6Ei6bC67g8k0IQZJpZ9RrFepi4XAeyUumPiE1QzV7soApYRTL39v9gEoGTcrMo4hriqHCDCdLw==> . It's the use case every mobile marketer dreams of: Make 'em stop while they're moving.

The departures of Mr. Iler and Mr. Forbes were voluntary..." Browsing Future

 

Mozilla's executive chair, Mitchell Baker, talked to CNET about what the company is up to and its expansion into mobile. She told CNET, "One thing that has shifted is the ability to access the abilities of the phone using Web apps. The new mobile computing environment is accessible and controllable from the Web. That is utterly Mozilla." The company also reported a huge bump in revenue, thanks to Google, from $163 million in 2011 to $311 million in 2012. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz-7P6cHH0KKfqgCB-PH8O6CqIsehDKIbZBtjTMk7CGgPlczJybXXm-5mAjnEC3xYUokvM2Ur8D4j2VvFCL52Y5-_ANFVyubFtyluBsTamGcxFPJGjLmobW0GmGyesGQrXArvlnj2viYv-TjAY3wnTLqKxDGREwm0phfvOVoJo7vUkRPfwBWLjexoO3uU74OQx2KitauF95BvjY8TMA3IRi0pAI9b4UfYE4=> .

 

Slow Holiday

 

Retailers are showing holiday ads earlier in the season, but the volume of holiday ads has decreased by 8.2%, according to AceMetrix. "The ads are a little lighter on the music, a little heavier on the background decorations. It's a more subtle way of saying the holidays are here than to hit them with big Christmas trees," Jonathan Symonds of AceMetrix told Ad Age. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz9cpGsaOvG1ubOAiU1CBds_6oqN0ueT0GdfGML3QciIcNW34y7dhNQfvoVVlF7SbO65hMkDDqWTgzc_A4SQbc0qpns8ggksH-OVJoaGTsugYs4uJC4UOPPkOKx1ipCMDVBN2Zf0c7L3QGMPfRr5h4KA57np9o4bpPB8WfPwvyUKB_665e_XEg6AlG6wd33ycsVyFdguWUhONA==> .

 

Video CPMs

 

On Digiday, Josh McDermott reviews The New York Times' investment in digital video and how advertising picks up the tab. McDermott writes, "The Times, which declined to disclose the cost of its ad inventory, could charge anywhere between $25 and $40 CPM for pre-roll ads on its site, according to ad tech executives. One exec said that the Times might be able to command a video ad CPM at $50. (...)." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz__Awncz65quRo-liRE24d1fB1WufRs9REYqNUeL1fl5UzT_LE2CJv6Q1ojUpefp4U3QJQ_DxJ1pGPiRkJl0aMOzpVr4bwfyWeCmoe8VA6fWZ7hB-o6MvdU3nKKdSSvJ6gF_5_csakt_xB3zL2xULifBNwnzCooOE8=> . Meanwhile, eMarketer ran an interview on Friday with NY Times CEO Mark Thompson, who reiterates the video emphasis and says, "The important part is working hard on premium custom advertising. In addition, we're very focused on building video advertising and on taking a more proactive view of programmatic." Read that one <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz-CYjffIKdwsCU6FM-7Xo64cGILqX4-nHWrn0QQKO3hQx56HzAnvkKfsOv05Oqsb8TASudFs9g4UFlJgkFa3ska0tpWlmbrBP7t71m3RpJ1VnhAEZ_ObT0AntJBzFzlFQqBM1u5H18wOxQeRD2t_VrERoivC8ewNm_Eg7l-Ne3RtOfB8lfXMYAeYuH2AfnoJ1zI2L80hWtLrIglo-60tz71Gg1_uRQjGh2dCTi-unL4h-wc3EeIc4Dl> .

 

Tracking Search Marketing

 

On Business Insider, Adchemy CEO Murthy Nukala discusses the "state of" his marketing tech company. Nukala reveals that his company has 30 clients using its new search marketing product and says that average budgets range in the $200k range. "Adchemy's new product is intended to structure a retailer's online catalogue so that it responds with product listing ads in Google by extracting that meaning, rather than by simply matching keywords," writes BI's Jim Edwards. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz9X0evcTXeLS75hI4-35Urnw_hVV_XqIXOpSz0PC_DmZYK68St5-5i4W3ZfCS67VhTlMUrAROmsdhqoaLGrHOn3zBrV0qjHFq-Erwn1_bKRwmJz6YeKi26pGCssvmTzsC8zN0Mh5GZATWrrrQhGthLUlzexvQQTuAA=> . And read AdExchanger's interview <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz9Q0DM7nLSBjPK4Zynr7xatGk91RLBFB-J9RdbCeB8F8LS75hDqjV6k8YNHhjo8zZ8Q5PMNilJbixPI7qNGjvrxSwXa7TLLsp2YAGFHLILN_KCTKOJe1IITN_nG03a6a3F7mlZoPD010hm-_ZICTQ5MKAUEpVYe3CwyEloslCWt9iUfUDw8AB4cUPjJHxd441y9bBBXQDU55NSZttSxa_8QOk2TUmY2qZM=>  earlier this month after Adchemy sold its lead-gen biz to XL Marketing.

 

Leaving AOL

 

Nathan Richardson is stepping down as president of AOL Live, according to POLITICO, only two and a half months after taking the position. Richardson was working on a live-streaming video channel, and a program called "770 Live From AOL," which is now on hold. AOL didn't give any comment on the situation. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz_JsdX9Wc4ghstN1-BPrZTlKI66kXCSZtRAu8jyvmsnSSv_NTdZZjyYjJGmnjYMexpMGwp2K6toTvYaudQh6DZgASNbPh9tWBncb2waWzIL-nIiB9a9UAOJSt2fDtyo9iVIDfr8wAvrksZZbfl6-U3mDn8fJKHgexlnGN6A4cr4S3DpvMZmRVirBup73asfBMyGly2IZOdl6w==> .

ComScore Rankings

 

Late last week, comScore publicly announced the October rankings <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz_Ke83lrYQmRaYQcRM5Yx9CAMeZMT1IR6t-PQ4gpctpVaqRMTtovSW-iG5SMz40sJal9U2qK_mqrYvJguXgp2Og2hQxXRimucO1Z5Xu6XBELbVLtHnh1HdCPG7SRDT4BYtuSD9nJUFjQQLNmMM6Uu5t4neZXjqdGnBn4TgpC9ROPLcR5f_NnO5lGrplW7djyiNOCjJAK5oqdAUwEJx1OpMqPCc8CDvjc-1ulHOp0QYTXe1zBRwbXRCLVkFIMYDAWUQ-jOMrcJl7qA==>  - by U.S. reach - for its pay-for-play ad network list known as "Ad Focus." Among the highlights, comScore saw 225 million U.S. uniques in October, it's breaking out "desktop-only" traffic and, finally, it looks like retargeter Criteo has decided not to pay to play and has dropped off the list (but was on it in September <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001GJ_rzJqGlz_Ke83lrYQmRfgO6APLaCe3RoTsaBE6GvwkhDj8dcQtUNJazvXkPDxCOGJ5b6ecZPqwk6N2V3kajirBqNiEezkAYorXWVDsOnhKUNVe_WMyrG-iBQW-WKMkApCBWEUgYa1v3FGM_5j-ujVB4xqF1reqsYg3XTnbcaz5fSvQ8r3KOHekdMlZanld1GDi8SfdHyDOfoHXRSJ_hdpitawA112dS5c668qPwR0nDYSZLgyJzlUpYLL8s9nlNELhZaoXfqg=> ). Could this signal a strategic shift by Criteo?

 

Mobile Adoption

 

IBM conducted a study that found 90% of global companies are willing to sustain or increase their investment in mobile technology in the next 12-18 months, according to Mobile Marketing Watch. "It is far too limiting to define mobility simply as a device or a channel for transactions. The organizations that come out ahead will be the ones that prioritize mobile and redefine its use to drive a new set of business expectations and user experiences," says IBM's Kevin Custis. Twitter Targeting TV (Again)

 

In a blog post yesterday, Twitter continued its TV-online product drumbeat and announced TV conversation targeting for US and UK advertisers. The post explains, "The way TV conversation targeting works is simple: Through our conversation mapping technology, networks and brands can promote Tweets to users who engage with specific shows, whether or not a brand is running a spot in the program. Now advertisers can easily reach Twitter users exposed to integrations, sponsorships and other innovative TV tie-ins for an additional touch point or message expansion." Surely, the reach extension offering of "targeted conversations" through MoPub is on the way. Read the post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5HWRmUkapVkX79hjYuLiy_rj_ZxzTlFoA--KHLCgd31AVkVltr5S4uvGLzYfxJVJ94adNdUPUBfBxl0J5A-k1xYqYYfzG7w-grw3NvxpazJa-LK1R5_3_55_wysNCdUH3UyB1WgrvdJpX4UDwJtlRFSymIg_kPiDHc8c_LQAK-A5c4TrWa_wA1se-puZs6yDTtwT_ebS98MadNHSy824q4qM3TQC2QtnodmNXZx8bRJ80awG9c1sNyu> . Now that Twitter is public, let the cavalcade of ad products begin. It's time to monetize.

 

Matomy Makes Mobile

 

Through its own mobile ad tool called Mobit, Israel-based Matomy Media Group is using real-time ad platform AppNexus to reach mobile users, says Adweek's Garett Sloane. Matomy CEO Ofer Druker explains to Sloane, "Most times when you want to buy traffic on mobile, you can't buy from one source lot of traffic. Mobit is one system to buy traffic from multiple sources." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5HIyHckCclpqaCIGIyjoR77AFW3e1i5d2TzWOlo-9EcnI8_MWxgcXPmvTkF_xyHV2CpHDzQrxnpftCtKLW0eqETQq7aNL8RXK4NXWNut6OgclKbsQ50ERsJG7szx_C6vzcE3yTKldcQnjG3xULsga21spAU98SGnPbqPZPti9LN5TPu6ybD_nX71mQo30zmrVpjnx2ei3ycSRLS6El64GSFnw0WpcoN_ss=> .

 

Whither Transparency

 

MediaPost's Gavin O'Malley reports from one of his company's conferences where Starcom exec Tracey Paull says that transparency is a challenge in real-time bidded (RTB) auctions. Quoting Paull, O'Malley writes,"'It's a little bit [like] people like it to be complex,' [says] Paull. Needless to say, agencies continue to demand transparency, but Paull likens the effort to a game of Whack-A-Mole. Wherever the agencies start to get 'clarity' in one area, opacity rears its ugly head somewhere else in the system." Read a bit more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5FetbIZ0FCum1djhg88foQr3pCge6ZyMZyem_sPPApyGxLR-RxVIeGUpa7Kg-lzqunxzWorD7BVIFFthi4cV4Nn7UezJwucXfdcbwW1iw9N6_eIuETBlYONIEQbwqfCxlGqNR2fUy4eQUNhFuoCQUWSxzKaAlHKJHJM4zyMBjDegkTFPVs_95jagny3lwQDX2EmLjl2KU7dzl2V9G7u57CXwPVlbRcZRY8=> .

 

Please Note: "Marketing" Platform

 

Google continues to talk about its array of solutions as marketing, not just advertising, in a promo piece on the DoubleClick for Advertisers blog. Google doesn't want to be pigeonholed in the paid channel -- it wants to be a part of the earned-owned conversation, too. Read the positioning <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5E9MWzGysi_m2GB7d7pUgfqbWG5SkuMsA3k13_XS_PTylcxmQl-9zMyF-Mf05GqY_wNKwhvL32eL9O0nu6NlSBs92xHSTGSxTS__4YIBkfsbI2DBAKGCHkLL_YF5dB95rDp6cZSH5tUNC2w2RusazEbAUbRXaPwrAs56OKLxZxKfEIgCY_W3Q3Q0OM88tV0CcfMl4B0DGSrXlpmqWnEY0bm> . Companies like Adobe, Oracle and Salesforce are in this battle with their various formations of marketing clouds. Is the Google Marketing Cloud on its way?

 

Native Vs. Programmatic

 

Emarketer takes a look at "native sponsorships" with some original data and sees irony: "The growth [of native sponsorships] comes as more advertisers rapidly increase spending on highly targeted programmatic inventory at the expense, in many cases, of more costly premium placements traditionally found on the homepages of large newspaper and magazine websites."

Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5HJMzaqHSl5RGCDGUPmh7HNJNLge4MT4caa4_BuaetaFa2dU8v12ISza5N-Xqx3I5W7eY-yk4AAs5MeQbucqlG4xuTKOPwEhqcSK16r0e2gFK0oc5rFZRYEIWWx3suK5E7G9ittWZHy8N3agBbmqZO6vqP8S7CjMeurehRtbdsUawMRiNxFzI5ZifM-x_7rOBEU23_wX1168w==> .

Engaging Social

 

Social-engagement and curation-tech company Livefyre has acquired realtidbits <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5HSaI_qlBE-SBu9HtF3vZ46H6MyEyLXbUvT1NlC6TupiTrzvUtxhbBKwSgSeVOHJ4XhVi1azXR2Dv7Ke9jW4p8EqmZ2cqITbyKFesIsMG59aw==> , which is positioned as an analytics platform of sorts. According to TechCruch, Livefyre CEO Jordan Kretchmer believes "the acquisition will allow Livefyre to not just [understand] data around social media engagement, but also video engagement and second-screen engagement driven by TV shows." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5E4-DkH9g9Xk67KkhPhEuEpz_D3YJjuQYHICjAWOS8VWiorYm_Ckto5JTStIolCAT2WJXVGOnAHOF1Swd-iwUHECJdHOnNTmUu56npyumSZsU2cPRvyt97RHkDFQSsGT3brazcnx9fq7-EYcjrMjDCPnr5-y-RpP7sCjj3WUt1amg==> . And read October's AdExchanger interview with Kretchmer <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5G0raAnSqzACGQJOba2mv_VU_CD_2sQn6M3W0ebGPePir6bmYZU6wo1XysqCKRydx9yf187a7dFKsq8CfpwYJBOG5T-UWYx3DWNxx7zlUn1BM-m5o52sS6qBIaSdFjDFT084GumbgsuGFfzpK7VEgNk> .

 

Privacy Box

 

Tor is repackaging its privacy-centric router for consumers, allowing them to obscure their online activity and block online ads for $49, according to the MIT Technology Review. The Safeplug doesn't guarantee anonymity, though, as users will still have to disable browser plug-ins, and Web-based services may still collect information that is typed or sent. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UdWYKZ4VC5GeD77NazMPGqoPCySZTvVn68BxBxc0R_hmO0MFzCoIurdBNdjztKG_0bjLXGe0hiLBYQ2_HbTwFlvs9IJW7EuPZVzgkHLMYZi7iqmtWQmXYCQeFPoDC39Yw_tMPhF9lzLR_WIq6x5nIOr326HL0S64KfxCNsG19C3NyLgPWK9ctxPedZdbbsMxo5cB8tDxQXU=> .

Paid Hire

 

PR company Edelman has hired VivaKi AOD's Chris Paul to helm its budding paid media practice, according to Ad Age. "The volume of paid work we're doing is increasing," said Kevin King, global chair of Edelman's digital practice group. "It's happening organically." A lot of that paid media is being driven by social, King told Ad Age. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001vFBRLYBQ-YE6nh7FEz-TTKf5jqz5XogXCF4BzxMu6oY_JKVCHYnmqGAY89gffu4AkoLnmU5LZfClkUMRjVbzVCG6zfZ3YCNFnNPQVLIFqNbqGvOJTXIX8RbzYLD2kgUIJVCWpJ93Oa0FrzBbWgWHx7GlKtktLaINWsYHCx2vqlwJOAfrsXf-3-pu_zcUB7a7n4DZmz-vTA4xHjIPen2mpZCOk3UkW7Vn> .

 

Shopping Beacon

 

Shopkick is capitalizing on Bluetooth Low Energy, which Apple included in iOS 7 as iBeacons, to bring shoppers discounts for products they are interested in while they are in stores. The technology isn't new, but the retail application is. Macy's is a closed beta partner, but the service will open up to others including Best Buy and Target, according to TechCrunch. The Shopkick API will allow companies to customize which deals, alerts and loyalty points are sent to a customer. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001vFBRLYBQ-YEm8Y-He3YmiXQ912st1FsDl5yTbZ9HS-EZ4LixAmqxnfF5rz6m7skLKx-RqoI4KSPdhQG-9RS4_AgG8OUoK1stdtGI5tKj-3M4euGMMThDjcX7HSTcHAcHslQSm0llxCXdCiNUXeaD3qN5_YOTFMApzOm2mjh8k7SoDyIqtwtbCH1LDbY-tfNCxClXuSDSre50dZFqg7tpEDqUasLuIpPytQ3ErATpgjCyoyZg8c5aPE9iV_OIYQpgGoE5PXLwr619AlrYpD1_kg==> .

 

Social Steals

 

Snapchat has turned down multiple billion-dollar acquisition offers because it thinks it's worth more. PandoDaily's Alex Park agrees, reasoning that Snapchat offers one-to-one marketing opportunities that even companies like Facebook can't match. Snapchat won't replace Facebook, but it can certainly take a slice of its market share, and that's why interest is high. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001vFBRLYBQ-YH8C-vfLcdcqdjCGTw8Z-DcABZeYC8r11f_xwfE3KGxIWHSflQW48Y_gES6iWwIN_0qROmmisxeVho9Z39Ho21xiCLxdvyDh1x7cFSZDN1dqIKmyH1MiOINRXJ0So26spKCcKkx-Vb6ARkgqByZRCnb5NX4Iuipn5FC-mkf4MCAoGmL4RhWFZ1B> .

 

T-commerce

 

Australian retailer Glue Store has locked arms with ShopReply to let users buy clothing featured on TV through email, text or Twitter. "We believe that Twitter has the propensity to become a significant ecommerce channel capable of processing enormous transaction volumes by leveraging massive real-time TV audiences who are already tweeting, giving these audiences the ability to transact in real time when they are emotionally engaged in content," Brad Linderberg, the CEO and founder of ShopReply, told Australian publisher CMO. The company has also worked with magazines to allow users to shop directly from the pages of the publication. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001vFBRLYBQ-YGYX1_j_PBgOfIf8S7L9QhgByQ9a5GCszoyl7n3UuKP7SLStWm0McPSgOH-flO1edHuHpFXowJyRDaW8SgjLscZC3qJCvF7rHvQ0fLs5WNRfTQkkVGQFY4NX2m_2C43iFBxkmYQS19vtzjg3_mLMOyfmIJegHrU2WSLcHTDwwuM1dhPjWq6Hmi3PP1ZUUoWPLE=> .

 

Viewability Update

 

Marketers will have to wait a bit longer for the Media Rating Council's (MRC) blessing on viewability measurements. Instead of lifting its Viewable Impression Advisory at the end of this year as initially expected, the MRC says it will do so in Q1 2014. After spending roughly a year reviewing vendors' various methods for determining whether consumers saw an online ad, the "key remaining issue is to reconcile the viewability measurements of different vendors," according to a released statement. "When that is complete, the reconciliation process will make it possible to explain and fully understand differences in viewable impression counts." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001vFBRLYBQ-YG6P_S7LhTDVn8H8T2aTpyxM1Iol-SG8wgAs5hj-5n17JqLgoeUfGDpMnigpnPd3rZPfFBuo4B92GrEPSDwaRGJPO_L-lv1lPWc0ZdyRuI8tp2fd8WEfDQXlhwTm5y_hdJoQAsS30Nm1wA31qtotgKg08GcBdqFAnPy2bWC_p_U0AFWNArxIFysmf9DcM1BnrM4D-aon0ug8exYUPG3RD_D4jUdlZ-0K-k=>

Pandora's Ad Network Issues

 

In Digiday, Josh McDermott reports that there's been some shady mobile ad network business happening through the ad network connections of music service Pandora. McDermott explains, "Thousands of Pandora users recently opted in to a push notification asking them to share their smartphone calendar information. Pandora insists the push notifications were not associated with ads Pandora sold directly. Rather, they were served by an ad network used to fill Pandora's unsold inventory." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TSP4ou9TS3cMYkZyXS_VDwSqu9WKnjbZLKITcfJOMfNZ-QYR3ZH6b5n14ya_dlpVkFfjK8POmzrsKI3lh-CD3GY-kk3X7dw313rHBcCiF94dY3YoeinFMY2Fvhtctyuog-XU3EvoRmDpFskp6o7WVpK1UzWzF0lQX5R_lv00rxs=> .

 

LinkedIn's Native Products

 

LinkedIn announced <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TSP4ou9TS3cuJmXhzopA-9UvJQJkXgxu76-OtSSak73TgftsK1vkkiWqNc2_DXOjSxCabK2thPrnvwQzwLVnSmbDtWqUZcWjHtgF_xDkv-fb7IxmxCm6TkK5YOPYVkm_G9JFLbvNtCfy929Pmt9VjU3rPgHV1Bu3dfJgLzb0DAncp5lUaK2IFlzGiuTJbU6f>  a new Showcase Page option that opens up more opportunities for companies to put specific brands in a consumers newsfeed, opening up a chance for more native advertising. The tool is launching with Adobe, HP, Microsoft and Cisco as partners, allowing these companies to build standalone pages for specific brands such as Office or Adobe's Cloud. Users will be able to follow the Showcase Pages the same way they follow company pages, and they will come with their own reporting tools. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TSP4ou9TS3f-ot3lxZmX6DQPaoQCY18IGp3XjlFeom6Ac20u-4SXJJIXwVBIfg-qlSPQi7MZqBtNTRHqurPP1JNzvLNOoFblR1WWaePGFUznYCR8jYVNtobOitVMtwUf1TgsYMUeE_Se_k9GVu-S32ZWY4oButaucTtYuIOiCMnD-vhqqW_TKjkM1sKmoZDpK-zvo31758TH07-chBCXlw==> .

 

Hearst's Data Business

 

In its business category, Hearst's focus on data services (via investments in Fitch Ratings and Black Book's auto database, among others) has helped buoy the whole company. "Our focus is on data and analytics and software used by our customers in their day-to-day operations," CEO Steven Swartz tells Crain's New York. "These businesses have a very strong growth rate, as there is more and more demand by businesses to use data to make smarter decisions. And [we are] looking to acquire more." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TSP4ou9TS3ex4KbFgLNWgClhgih5ggnqRbzB15X3l20Ow2PXWc5h6EpOFFBEEO_z4j6Kq8dUZ32hQmP9i6ns2TFswE5zELD-b469KFRVEObKrHtopTGqp8ddffv5hh47vmU5CO6vHk3W4e62azdIdM-JYS6oXFml2li6UUEMznKbvSAXX2gDz8Y3uubSLF51> .

 

RTB A-Go-Go

 

Mobile DSP StartMeApp, which says it has a huge presence in Latin America, announced that it's launching an RTB exchange. On the client side the company has worked with companies like Coca Cola, Skype, Audi and Fox, and on the publisher side it has worked with Rovio, Reuters, The Weather Channel and more. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TSP4ou9TS3e6BRTOWEbCsWwSuwTK1RJXgThZCJx3gpsGWU1WJ43BS4DIoKgOd3UA46sO-2EWXYsAw-LxtSH6DzbpmcvdB5Jvo1eaa4QwpE54ncN1k3RDhgSigoqrbplS0G_W5vfBn__5zQhaZfYIGVIyHdU2wM8QptP8PEGkejeLljCoTa24m-_f54gufXlpmMkEkNnExio=> .

 

By The Local Numbers

 

Local advertising is slowly going digital and, according to a BIA/Kelsey study, digital will account for around 20% of local ad sales in 2013. As MediaPost points out, mobile is going to have a very high growth rate, as local mobile ads will account for 37% of total mobile ad spend this year. Although print sales will continue to decline, online newspapers should remain steady, but radio and TV won't account for much local spend online. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TSP4ou9TS3dzIe0PnH1b65CZWhCUlg__SAhKpPFPDiFvVp3DAI4IYe-saKbpsYjqtRKMSwkTvQan32wptgRD8NF4p2RZj6wj0fvcyWrokUQ3dkmd03_vp75XaxbnhyJ_j0MlLnYzAjhN4BThaYQDMrlXT9ikwPlubeGE65038NjzZiTdEOh38esK4u5N2AdniLoIcpwx6M4_-MzW7LquBWZPgy15dYytohHLecobBm4=> .

Mobile Minefield

 

Although mobile ad revenues are increasing, not everyone is "killing it," reports Mobile Marketer's Chantal Tode. Velti and AT&T's AdWorks were both shut down as a result of not generating enough revenue in mobile, says Tode -- while Facebook and Google dominate the mobile channel. Julie Ask, VP and principal analyst at Forrester, feels consolidation is the future of mobile advertising, saying, "Mobile won't be stand-alone." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TSP4ou9TS3fmfgVl4RiT8UHaO53XasrUi7zcWDOvypGK8GBWQVWwGR7ymqoBdARN9kW1pm8NUsDDHWBWk8u56AGjeBO2HQnBnaanbWhdBybbUU3Cvj6jW1jSOlrgiY2oV_U2NutSBcG98LLH_DTs9MwEKhq2EDEUCR2IzQTlCChtP6-6M62yDg==> .

Programmatic Video Upswing

 

Programmatic video is growing, but it's not likely to overtake traditional buying for a couple of years, Magna Global North America President Kristi Argyilan told Ad Age. "Programmatic direct or private marketplaces, they have definitely crossed the chasm. We're seeing it in the most-premium publishers that embrace programmatic, from The New York Times to Viacom to Discovery," TubeMogul CEO Brett Wilson said. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017PXpCsGI4TpgJxJbBliPiA-qFjoVDoPG-DnJ5c3ZI_fPekJ4Hfz2JMbXNqasmJVY5DQ8j7PBYlBOSJMsI8E-rJDLAHD8B7N5AiH_X-FlbOevcVi5ZGntXt9eELY4WKiJXfecg9_CYMwg4faNK4_gNCm9JA29bJ_WInMnXE2MyNHFZoETtPOsDf44NGO_-58QImEozIWla7A3j0DYW28pIg==> .

 

The Future Of Ad Tech

 

The advertising industry continues to change, and AOL's Bob Lord makes five predictions for the future on Harvard Business Review. The biggest change, which is already well underway, is automation and consolidation. Efficiency will be the name of the game as open ecosystems win out over single, niche solutions. Mobile, and multiscreen advertising in general, is already changing the way advertisers and marketers plan and execute campaigns, and that's only going to increase in coming years. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017PXpCsGI4TrtG6hsEmSZMfe0DGQHfnNSBXwRvdBwefukZbeAbU8Nh8YqPf33R9wAjCPjpWKvlkMpcpAFPKCc4B2Nc0IyY2Ax0rptch3Odvrc73_qeF-0aFUmAopsTFugGJYCP0Ndv38lNmj5aDlALOBF5E2QGpRdltGwwA4-bP-LpQHDzKBDqR4PKdqQb1aSUsIIYuL_j8uKFiXZtHywtQ==> .

 

The Heroic Banner Ad

 

On his Searchblog, Federated Media chief John Battelle ruminates on the "heroic" banner ad and writes, "One generation from now, we may not 'click' on banner ads, but we'll always be pulling into traffic, filing health insurance claims, buying clothes in retail stores and turning up our thermostats. And those myriad transactions will be lit with data and processed by a real-time infrastructure initially built to execute one pedestrian task: serve a simple banner ad." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017PXpCsGI4ToTb4zQ4iW-9jYvy3h-uundKRKxHMiXtMGL6TVwog37fSVCWH3SYEYDO3x39-U-L8RiwZ4u4Aw0mnIbxfURQ1g46Wg8l-gv0T8Ee5irraHhs8X48nvrNCQzqzxXbfuysl8csEXNCf7LJhf74jHVZROwZtRvE4DdzfcbpNAY5dsHTEI4T9ND1iL4HO6k_0lm5PF7nACjgp8VdascoBz3x0UdfIpkFgoTWhVtraneB7yJiADjrWvIq3Dw> 

 

Scan Suit

 

Yahoo is being sued by users who are upset over the company scanning their email in order to serve targeted ads. According to Bloomberg, the plaintiffs are seeking $5,000 for each person who says their privacy was invaded. Yahoo won't comment on the lawsuit, but this isn't the first time a company has been sued over (contextual) scanning of emails. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017PXpCsGI4Tq2ERzwiomWLxykluMjNlg5fsQ4LNOyTzZPjFkDcT0kz8PBQbHzxXgJskx-UBF0vh7FxrGSrwKfSuptjfBeJzNrz5QSqP3-3XvgdM8LYf4VRfoM5KtphooGkcx_nAfYA1kN5KRb1G3uKPnou7237xsiPih85SiD1EETnaiMkRDXj1zjFXf8706_shY3LSnh2wIhJSWtv-G-tj6NtNuVTMwzTY0EE4DVxCY=> .

 

Vimeo Scale

 

Reuters' Jennifer Saba reports that Vimeo has one-tenth the scale of YouTube as IAC execs "opened the kimono" on its broadband video destination website. Saba writes, "IAC revealed that Vimeo has an audience of more than 100 million unique users, 400,000 paying subscribers and about $40 million in revenue over the past 12 months ending October." There's a business model there somewhere. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017PXpCsGI4ToaqgHC8UegQyTu478lPIkgbr-cooz03fke1vj2LEYXF9IHvMsU0hCMfVEe50kyagoadlPsyKZaLq0DGF2WwdGooc8wkX2LqyD32tYyFpIOR9ckNoMFje14pJ_93QNSFxwxSMYnHEXgoVqTfRO3P2ikKJrMLurZpncWNdgNHAb6pz_97VBarSPGl719Oi-UuY0=> .

Programmatic's Hot Stock

 

Jim Cramer invited Rocket Fuel CEO George John to his CNBC "Mad Money" TV show on Friday. In the process, Cramer offers his take on why ad network 2.0 Rocket Fuel has been successful in the public markets: "Programmatic online advertising is smokin' here and so far there hasn't been a good stock that's allowed you to profit from this theme." See the interview <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA0gwU-9zCMIEbV7B2MkAfAxHoysQD2pcY3vi9kE9OB1F7xFXxLTd0ZU4oUoCUP-Lv5owSbl3TYGzxBIcl8agGx-MWaEb7YQakyi7uHJSbpHWrh4ygoIY8FN62_Pcizmvsy7X41fjISWDDLqBKZCfULZyLUy8LBbGk4=> .

 

Data For Advertising

 

Facebook updated its privacy policies on Friday with changes it first proposed in August, reports The New York Times' Vindu Goel. Goel simplifies the change thusly: "By having an account on the service, its 1.2 billion global users are allowing the company to use their postings and other personal data for advertising." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA1TN1t8NZ2j9rrCIz0T5-7nKcj0ppSxXcsfprY22LIaLVIkRMx2EztX1NdI0IAzNt0ET_DsQq5_Pv9XoU1sr_wfnPD_NK7HITjPEQQnCLylQjOW5SYkb3ONBsFRZzuJVUDTIHM2BIfVySTFevF8oKQM_4Z92Cpo78WRriWh7hbXOMcmCmxaSkB6paaVwUfRZ01zupbVvpfkLg==> . The WSJ Digits blog notes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA2q9Mi055hL6iyLzkRmFb3Y3ih9lpyqEH_XyXBmI-z3yS4SrOdZJT5Dm14Hl-D0Q2c92qIkBQfZmmYdry505Sg2eV4rzjLtIc2dKIN-yN02RgdkWp_G--gxFkfyp7OCYY6vrmZ1dpvleo0_rgMHYzSu4TrckOC08vWJTRQ1ML6ntOPfe3t6UsZ9jUXsWBZ5QjPX-mRc1aGGGIwdII-5WAHmNh42TXLXbHg=>  a controversial emendation about teen use of Facebook has been withdrawn.

 

Mobile Marketing Automation

 

Silverpop is releasing an SDK for mobile app developers, according to The Next Web. The SDK will also tie into Silverpop's database to give developers analytics about users. The software allows for personalized marketing messages through mobile apps, and will let developers follow up through email and other messaging. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA0c3uiYl-z2NFm8e3KxVpfMBJN-Wsmrt1yH7x-OccpZ7YDE_Va6c-gnWS_vrdfTZF8tjR_RuDrHpeHTxIus1YJlqcccBchhVUbf18ouGAjd-H1g-TIssfFjLgq-U4PXW0qIxcDVQeVfekZU0zGDj90f_mZ2edQHlxbsJOR7KXJI8bL0ZES8H_K8Qc8648NAX1bsAqUdcAseCKgmOK3Rc8aXCeDHbReAHPWksuSzTx2reeHUR1clot2eJEvY6ukI2kirGbJpSyiu89BPnP2NbGqU> . This move reminds an editor of Mopub's SDK proliferation which led to its acquisition by Twitter.

 

Forbes For Sale

 

According to a staff email, Forbes Media is up for sale. A New York Times reporter's source says the company could garner up to $400 million from the sale. That's more than WaPo. This isn't the first time, and probably not the last, that a high profile sale like this has occurred for a legacy publication. The New York Times Company and The Washington Post Company both sold off major publications to private owners. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA0ig4Yzsl2qhjZ7XvBQzPp1htHK1f1sPNWqB4N3JHRmUxoO3ZRC1Y2OC16vHwCYKqXfI7P7Yp1HvnohFqSW2CgkdnCM5LcdsDsGpCv8cEnTGjVlsAZCnwGCvo0MbJ7bC52F65Jhqf1fb4jujssF6TGqH4_XrdGUq0vM5nA3boLqniGxN2XO02ZAYN04sSPfMZDORetRZP7B-Q==> .

 

Mobile Ad Net Machinations

 

Mobile ad network and tech firm Millennial Media's stock price plunged <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA3qa2-ZB2UL4edNbTHUSDPvE0TssaSycOsww_YPx5rrnno6tq9hLnsuh0qnMVAMiba9MW68pZfs4u_bbKhc1xCPOXm7vw14uMLmNgm4ou5fvFuMSPP16YvvZ3Z62xgNkW7yz7iGuz2DPNlK7aNLOGX2>  last week due to a near-breakeven outlook on future earnings. That plunge has pricked the ears of Goldman Sachs analyst Heath Terry, who has started coverage - albeit with a "neutral" rating. Is the "smart money" getting in to Millennial? Finance news site Benzinga quotes Terry's note to investors on Millennial's earnings: "While the acquisition [of Jumptap] expands the company's reach with advertisers and developers and extends its programmatic capabilities, we believe third party ad networks remain challenged as first party advertising platforms and their native advertising models drive innovation and share gains in mobile advertising." Read a bit more on Benzinga <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA2hcbVwb76p_SnrnFO6_HCa3C0L-fnoFgnncUL_jewAyYU_c89mukFRgb0-rK-u4wRMUb7bHewhJfkN8QrqSu3YHgBAvJ7KlBItlLmkbF5cAm__y7wsSJg1pbokEs75tbT2ptTj42XGEykk9YDd1pJh2UHLcc3GOtw6x0fTbC6msyxyFvMQBlz_o--41EGoesgGxfn45LZ9z-lOBBYqnggi5_H25WxOXiKiSjPickSwA_6KpdnNomyNllHAdhfGOyU=> . With Millennial's current market value of $500 million, the company would appear to be a ripe acquisition target itself.

Addressable Reach Theory

 

It's not an ads story explicitly, but you can now log in to your favorite Windows OS using your Facebook login. The Facebook Developers blog explains <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA38DzO_asLeuk9PS7y2WbDHZ9wJHtqZvS8WI_CTa6s4anNz_Fy78QSdBKQY9xOiRrpySqR5IMrv2nxtC0AKtSRvj_3HzPQ9Kk94cLndkvyaCC2wq_gi6Rv7HXrtU6sIRceJ7E34j6QPj178OIUHuWh4hMEQh-MM1rsjZCXP5eo8ZrhXTtNMxgDJotTv7yRTF24MQAfoPhtSKtdycXrBE8ReG3zDs-gny8r3SM6ajZrE_Pe78BpsrRIF4LgYJ3_wyyg=> , "Facebook Login for Windows 8 is ready to use in production apps, while Windows Phone 8 support is being launched in beta." In time, login data could - in theory - enhance addressable advertising opportunities across Windows and on Facebook.

 

Billion Dollar No

 

When Snapchat turned down a $3 billion acquisition offer from Facebook, it left some wondering what the messaging service has to offer brands on its own. Ad Age's Cotton Delo found a few examples, but it could be a tough sell initially. Right now it seems that musicians and movie ads make the most sense, if they pitch a product in a short window of time. Some food companies, such as 16 Handles and Taco Bell, have also experimented, looking to capitalize on SnapChat's young audience. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OAJbjiNAsA2oq8z3LH1s0Liwsz4Trry541sh6rcrWoT7ppmz5iFUezcXp48htzkRN04keO7Aehyhe8KbcEFk7geaQ6DdRrrAlKcKzNwHMknEmsGXH1RdwnWX0rPVXoe5f8EMpK9i9kUyT_CDyZEAGeQg5MO3k6Y8K_9ksgiGBNYnxVfXtRrxYYEPUWs4m9kSWpUEz4DKTog=> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>

Pinterest API

 

Pinterest has been driving retail referrals like crazy, and is now offering an API allowing websites to display their most popular pins. According to a blog post, the API has been offered to BuzzFeed, ModCloth, Target, Whole Foods, and others. Read the post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JqJmk5EEOYf-tdbN5Mzi9HIyyaOYFU9QSkvqBdPOBQaN-cBWxCQswSREZUdfWz53AUiTw0leAUtVbAzCTguFLOJzJ1m8qrRIFNiMNd_ohUZ3EyFYzQ2Obj6uBUOIFrfX6XIhN2uyYX1mMb3HywVHS6jCXal2a522K9-S2lY8Jsm7tJpfiCfH06jiwSvdy6p5rIMUgukHiBWZ1Zy7VeWKixS6thIGiivk> . As Pinterest experiments with a promoted pins option, this could give sites the data they need to figure out which products are worth promoting.

 

Digital Upfront Gets Real

 

AdAge reports Publicis Groupe's Digitas LBi and Razorfish have committed more than $100 million for inventory on multiple Google properties. "Google wants to become a player in non-search inventory and grow things like YouTube," said Rishad Tobaccowala, chairman of DigitasLBi and Razorfish. "They have some capabilities to develop content, but that's not the business they really want to be in. We know how to make that engine run." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JqJmk5EEOYeegIKeTQ_AKyaIVNCSLwLPhDbbIr9drr2ciQ9OSDm0PvQ5zAsGh23RdDE2JZaSg-pdKE86DUaiNi-sSihNzjOysv9crAboXQwRLyeRHE_Fm917C16mbOWOpwzOie9Cxk8zMoRTawZ74w7n3YPPm-Vf0K8mKWMn6v_Z35507ZEXHWriAyURXOg9dol24Hyh9P3_4euOV6MBTXRF5WDd5XhJ> .

 

OneSpot Spots Some Cash

 

Content advertising company OneSpot netted $5.3 million after its A round financing. Mohr Davidow Ventures, known for betting early on tech startups like recent Wall Street darling Rocket Fuel, led OneSpot's A series. OneSpot's technologies are designed to blend content--either earned or owned media--with display advertising. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JqJmk5EEOYeL0g_3_u0K561b1vZSbysceQaLaHfvyzq1yh9L_iTurZx7qpckrsJYaK_nuaGreQa2ge2Q5F2q4Yq8NOgtpyRp274Lj8ddDjU8PJ-UUONCwY1hApzS-8QRiMX1LyXdswdbnXaUsCufngpLohOttcH53rKSezeOPvUQehFru7DnT1SnKq88XESjyXERzUaB9OsdnUlb7IV09oXEAzG1sHouU5t8WHjGQ8wVEGoas0v3OYRm_KnTbO5k> .

 

CMO Measuring Stick

 

Business analytics company Domo surveyed 301 marketers and found they aren't getting all they need from the available data. Part of the problem is knowing how to use it - actionable insights! - as well as keeping up with it. Although 83% see value in having real-time data, only 37% can access it in real-time. Furthermore, 54% of marketers surveyed are compensated for ROI, despite limited measurement abilities. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JqJmk5EEOYdLrBbw0FepcX4b4A_TN3m-0ABYou3O28U5Fdl1OGBfxrOSKD2TAUznNQAhW_BJ1flDgVMt2Omz1QFhsSl5tFsjyD6BytrB8GAVD_cKgcKVTL_PszdtmZgDBLYV2cqhapE-wB3Oyf4iYlySY0-GXFH8YAlDQG7ew6J9t3U54u8PhClzUqR1hRSzZlrf38UogDNbdaqTC4w9D3bTmSZBvcTH87IFnK-SsjDvjnZQhjQsV4QDOgwZG9sKIHCEA5Ji-gr6e9L4JUDIBA==> .

 

Twitter Ads International

 

Twitter has opened its ad platform to small companies in the UK, Ireland and Canada, The Guardian is reporting. British telecom O2 is working with Twitter to help advertisers get the most out of advertising on the platform. "We believe that it's our responsibility as both a large corporate and a digital services company to guide them. That's why we are investing our time, money and expertise in this new social insights platform," said O2's Ben Dowd. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JqJmk5EEOYcNd7JBbmUVNsgp1Z87w60-BY5AHOQv1AysOgwkXx7IHCRvRl6k1QUMfnXN4D2KqV4PNql14zKPLat6PRYuAkbJKG1KzeE5FlgFhOAhSNiV8_tgKc2V4IqB-acxnjyEcTAH8hYWl0vfJ4_fnjbcySdlmNNq6s3NKqDmAoFn0lWV9Jqt5tuXoEsUMvIjrn6NcSBEiIiin-e6qDQawnVymphPiwhjEGeQjcWqOJytm5IKVA==>

It Must Be Amazon

 

Many an ad technology company uses Amazon Web Services (AWS) for some part of its technology backbone. SunTrust analyst Bob Peck attended the recent Amazon Web Services re:Invent conference and came away impressed. He thinks AWS is a ~$3-4b business today and growing "north" of 60% per year. Peck adds, "In fact, AWS Senior VP Andy Jassay stated that [CEO Jeff Bezos] and the management team remain excited about the platform and 'that in the fullness of time' could be the biggest business at Amazon." More on the conference from ZDNet <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JqJmk5EEOYdTeawhgPGMj3FxhaDqZzCYrxl5A3O6ecp8ljd7gJ_9Zu4bU__TPTeNgNmG6rmCLOyqDagzdgFLshr7QSLhodv3nvZpBM4Eovgx-1k1_Q2PGbGrGvnXci96UYBA1n6pjq7EGDB2lnLVk68w2LyI8teAIAZWPzFUz30QM1UtLLAVDNKXZtu9Bhy3T_-sroWmuf59IJwgxnZvNf1tfmWG6eWS> .

 

In Market Buyers

 

On Marketing Land, Ginny Marvin notices that Google's AdWords platform has taken another step forward in attribution capabilities with a new feature called "In Market Buyers." She writes, "In-Market Buyers is an extension of the Interest Categories available in AdWords and represents Google's first attempt to make ROI a central focus of advertising on the Google Display Network." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001JqJmk5EEOYcAYURnmFCi6qLm2SrHp_58N2Crkmw7dnUoADnWgEQ4ZAwbKQyuJZw6Ihkty3XKElT9g4fmbTfkd-rU67qhVykqhRNpvyiKELf7p-Mfu_lxN7qwy_MtkrJPI2gaWOtr7RIkGLuFmPHj7-ugDQnnqjoZvCUXQIzVuhGSRO8aybr2Kh2R5m8ybOrfTyO0U2Aw8mU=> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017D_zG05Wu41SnqqoMGUJ8cRKRhZSrxzuT2EDAlWWPXkf0SjAXh1xKkkBUF8xTg-CbIjoqP4OpCIgqcTYajEHYfzOo3xUVUAfRZhFiupqs4gjtK5L24_dZhqz36Yx-HV9Alb3CDugWgU=> .

 

Native Time Inc.

 

Time Inc. is going to start serving native ads to more of its sites courtesy of Sharethrough technology, according to Ad Age's Michael Sebastian. Content is assigned a quality score, based on how much interaction it gets, so that higher scoring ads are shown more frequently to users. "We want to make sure it's quality content," Scott Miller, SVP at IBT Media (Newsweek's owner), said. "That's why we're not rolling it out to every single site. We want to ensure the reader is going to get a lot out of this." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017D_zG05Wu40Mmgo_7QQ5TN-QUVwmU1MSwfxThxC10xTLKEF468Pwgi0013bTJkKDjWLqhA1NS3FWFWcAqSq_mG0_2NFUEPG5M1o2zShrMMsM4F5EfNYra5GBUp0uwRfrn-VdqXzNPDBHqI6wWSzwBRgVFh6sDsuWPgZFjts6yF_ighl_7ik_v6rF2GOvMKMJJhC7J1fTwYk=> . Meanwhile, at the Wired Business Conference, PandoDaily reports that the NY Times' exec editor Jill Abramson called native ads "the buzzword of 2013 business model discussions at conferences." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017D_zG05Wu43ijBMTVtyXqG684ARdk7T_vxClubIB24nx3L6XCe4hOPagfjxGzhDx6aajKsWRR5vVJ8CgU4lkHCv73o-TxvEHlpTgEACWA5q03qNGIMYsOn_GbWoKCqXT5QMIMUpLyqQPEQ9QzJhqfTAUxcGyhGWlj_aa1NINM7QKyavSq0TG5a9Q55Y5080o477QQkKUvFg=> . Big publishers are desperate to stop the CPM slide.

 

Twitter Targeting By Device

 

Seems pretty basic, but Twitter announced that its adding the capability to target ads by device, OS version and Wi-Fi, according to a company blog post. The new targeting options extend to the reporting tools as well, allowing advertisers to make decisions about future campaigns based on those metrics. Twitter hasn't quite caught up to Facebook in terms of targeting options, but the company has been slowly adding on capabilities. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017D_zG05Wu43lKjsPCCz_BcjwrfqKXsZ7g2_kh8yWEOPkHKoEUeIUR373q-RypCg9bZrqqAEYoWyiAel7V6yYDUfN0Z8eC9c-50yFx1_LncPcX4VcM-0o2c5lixMewLs6jTbW53Q1vdl26oVajjFYYDi8yEij6Sqy20PX3adWH2IusENbUGhcw_UOSYo4jsMdgHEHYkthhgo=> . In theory, Wi-Fi should enable better targeting as AcquireWeb's Al Gadbut explained in an AdExchanger interview earlier this year <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017D_zG05Wu43488o79jvYDUsqBci13pT4BtRbGnpr4hWXO2WE424GT7B8q9AV-bTGFZlkkSjZrH5myh0fkgDVdrzw19T3DLjLq0I0I_9soq3uRm5EoWbgTBBGlWGl_iUrPnRJUvJA4jeEfYcNbBCQRVdXurrAjp2chqc33f_HGDvOaR0d5nDpDwT30VrRoa_k> .

 

Photo Performance

 

Publishers are seeing better performance with tweets that include images, Digiday is reporting, but it could be short lived as users' Twitter feeds become cluttered with pictures, lessening the impact. On Facebook, for example, some publishers find that text-only posts are garnering more reach than posts with story previews. "It seems like everything is trending towards photo tweets performing better as long as the photo selected is a good one," The Atlantic's Chris Heller told Digiday. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017D_zG05Wu422Reok9zStgcZfQnclGIvqwYqmW0Ks3hNvD0r2c5_SPW4g8puRWmUprpUSuio6_ieqwB1HSHkhPzvEK8fattmiNGCBKm4Q-k24u0reZNEayPEc4SiH0dnv2P7yCbZvNZEhfN1s2dR221VGIfX6L_NnWz2CjLKlV54=> .

 

Facebook Ad Performance

 

Add another chapter to the "Do Facebook Ads Work?" book. Travel trade Skift reports that TripAdvisor CEO Stephen Kaufer was "disappointed" with some of his company's Facebook ad campaigns saying at an RBC Capital Markets investor conference, "We weren't able to get the same traveler in shopping mode to come over to TripAdvisor in any scale that matched Google." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017D_zG05Wu41THeHDcyile9Ko7vRJf2HQ2yRlCJanB6ZZhUZK_LRM1oTKHKnFjn7BcCH6RB0rdSRKwYtP_V1t8QLqx88T7XvSAfXj2NaWn4rXqjuwFZyzkxmHHOjVLMd_Sy6pGbbDN0FDgeWpb-50HnJSESkCm_aOIRn4VcBatpBL5hxKr2NffDyRmZdjcUCKpKxg3R6wjxiVU6hkxfS9qSm_PHwe5DpA> . On the other hand, the campaigns to promote TripAdvisors new "Cities I've Visited" app were successful.

 

Brand Google

 

Google is adding on the marketing firepower with the hire of P&G exec Kirk Perry who was president of family care at P&G, and "was named president, brand solutions at Google, a new role reporting to Chief Business Officer Nikesh Arora," says Ad Age's Michael Learmonth. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017D_zG05Wu40XWbJO6trju6KyLOrPY6QPZ5HJE4mlycg0yOAAF7hs-qW9ZtCLl216fgY7cRoyZu0n1jzXucoiGWcDC7vkGeF8-yENgeRD9e4_WqlWe3e0_q97KrqZeEoBYS2p1Esxkx7OfFbc_BRDT9bGyLW3n4el4XcvE6JOycS5Y3DnbzuK9yglcvil7udIQGczJMk5CdqmvHMe1I14rN3qKcKNLjFj> . Learmonth says Perry will be targeting TV ad dollars that Google wants moving to online, i.e. YouTube.

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2FgqL1_fDVvAOdyYePAnxQT799ejjluXoaQb5d203V9y6GwlD29Pey5S7z0xma_iQhGjXooeqi_IACiqriPC_t3_l8wh1ybsnU7LsMdPWf2o-2NVBssR2pJaRESZg0W9V0=> .

 

No More Love For Cookies

 

Google is at work, along with companies such as Microsoft, creating a universal ID for users, but that could create problems for the industry, according to Adweek's Garett Sloane. Meanwhile, companies like Xaxis are working on a solution, called a statistical ID, which would collect anonymous information about users across devices and would level the playing field. "The advertisers in concert with publishers need to take a much more proactive role in terms of getting this situation solved," one ad tech insider said. "They can't leave it to Google." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2FPsrlDEUN5V3pL3WvkiLV2EbCPnF926_CxtTc7UedhQzqgwQ_9tgNbM7-1tE6veiBBrOTwcL8VryHbtAg6Hqy7eAC_3J_xhqPeSUlm6T99uT7T4qkpMQgm_ftEdwXWMMDR-sCkS1gpkUXv_Y4RE8eY3elHn6yOXcC1Ttcx-JYoVcZoESQUnyOEplwx-UJD3r8=> .

 

Nielsen's Shopping Analysis

 

Nielsen continues to extend its analytics platforms to online - this time by bringing its consumer purchasing behavior data to advertisers. The service will gather purchasing behavior online and offline to measure ad effectiveness, the company announced. "Clients can see syndicated data exposing the reach and frequency of their ads layered with actual consumer shopping behavior," stated Nada Bradbury, SVP Global Media Products, Nielsen. "Success can now be defined in growing the number of transactions and sales volume." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2G4C6crf9DVhMvzKfLuBJ3OheSwqxABI2dTW7l-O62cU6NNmqgJscDdgJG_q-V7cj_rO-tbc4Mk6nogqpTZSmoxu-hFqJXPjolTDIsagd2qFLPo-ff5pqVGKd7I4xvKNxrF3mJsTqYjXwf3SF5_Xb-UIxAzZGRFBa9qS6Yto4NMwyCNTBTnSwc9gdpD5xyq1llIbT2UHTGS1HPSvWid7Jp16cEb4IX7av7lLl3AKpxYhdulLCbAD7Q0f70rm_xybOc=> .

 

Fraud Aware

 

What does ad tech bot fraud look like from the publisher perspective? Digiday did a Q&A with what it says is an anonymous former publishing executive to find out what the process looks like and how it played out. The publisher claims to have knowingly bought fake traffic to boost its ad impression numbers. The company even tried experimenting with video, but found that bots couldn't load the players so it didn't work. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2GqP3FTcIxFVyG06jw39qJIL9Uxw71ujCAVU5wKgOQilUJ4VAVUtWU-QmpILxVB_SX_zRuZwlS-evaDxgsln1sjY34IAXszXc66-OqK4he954Zqq4RaIj9BJP7pM1bRKxKLswYxrX0vtDLfLxCeSyIKRdydsPCJ9Ig=> .

 

B2B Retargeting

 

Demandbase is launching a retargeting product for its "Company-Targeted Advertising" platform for B2B advertisers. "By using a solution specifically tailored to the B2B buying process, we're giving businesses the opportunity to influence multiple people involved in a corporate purchasing decision, at the specific target companies most likely to buy," said Chris Golec, founder and CEO, Demandbase. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2HUMcA8WPYg35zYtGsSrQUoEGpEGmOks-j_I31pgOrGHeus1CL6bx2S942F7zG8ytPYKaTG9hjwRHVRkvuzVEH8Yl8FKR6Y4YtXDHBobQuME4uF8r5LWdp4StTql_4XVo1_AGJ28ipbufgAAuOndO4_F0LDwQCKYfpAQ9KhdZQv12FDoRYcbDMwIeYxStSQLxiM1HZ2gxdrpzxmTvWdjBuUcyCKBavFKYNyQ246aPpxDeZ0UL1z8kra9fBY3HtizmI=> . Golec discussed Demandbase's platform with AdExchanger last June <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2Fu7zg9Jyr_gDFFtZhb2QSuD6h_IV7l6Xto9q6vM2MAKK04YnCmA6OCDFMTG2FUGOTT0g32DE9lMgxRIr5W0ayuVHelqxfMiTZ46XrWiPHy9ZposuZq-8zqjA0VYWRtNo_GcmgwS32Q8_im3Z7AN3BR_cK7WXAhFJEx52t9FgTcV7qErr1mkjCEgRqYDrEK5eBdutyFL8GGFNk21C8ijfgxeYb9CVAWFRCvHjYoutTpIKISBWNgTI6R> .

 

Privacy Coding

 

Online privacy can be fun, at least to those who showed up for Evidon's Ghostery hackathon, which focused on building monitoring tools for the web. Some of the entries include data visualization tools that show how many ads were served in a session and an alert system for users when their autofill information is being used. There are two teams left vying for a spot at South by Southwest. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2GlpG3_0qNmPrBZTNw6QgndNGEGb2vOKH7SdWTvxeEshdPw9AYl_upWN1YTDVANsPK0wV1AYNTRHhRTEV863YDay2CHKZJENm9Jj8R8-dAX-akRXuARczn8bH1gnP4uHVLZQRU3fbAmSsrU9QiGvCCzD3fWqioIAAhv7KV39Ohz3krLFcbdi0XjL649Oae2JiMI9s5D8sWP7_RwhafzhVhLvd8CCAo3nLI=> .

Extra Large Medium

 

In 2005, Upstream Group's Doug Weaver proclaimed the internet more than just a "medium," but rather a platform, and that message is still relevant today, as he notes on his blog. Weaver says advertisers still think of the internet as one thing rather than breaking it out into its distinct parts, such as search, email and social media, which all need to be treated differently to be effective. Add mobile to that, and second screen viewing for good measure, and simply calling it a medium seems even more unlikely. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2H72nCe8xHoqy1CqCfNKti3tpfPHMsMHagwZ4MGs6DXFpFzh1M3ncHmLdw80b2-fkn753S9hMcrgGddz_w8ec5dTpHFe2yDhoIQfAyrA-xwKdI7pUifkBbOxs9J6H68siHBa9jfq1D2fg==> .

 

Commerce Adding Tech

 

Target is having a hard time competing with Amazon, so it's taking steps to mimic the services that Amazon offers, as the Wall Street Journal's Paul Ziobro points out. Some of these efforts include subscription services, streaming video and free shipping for members. Target is admittedly a little late to the ecommerce game, as the company was focusing its efforts on improving stores, expanding into Canada and starting a credit program. It's also competing heavily with Wal-Mart, which has focused on technology more recently, with its Wal-Mart Labs initiative. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qze6yS3uT2Fyw2j3Qlca_Y6Hlf3VADsNuHkVcqZeOes8wHwCLH1XKJCVE8REuQgMyMgW9_RwTnQPaikCcvG3cAkEYpRQDuPh637uqkotCNwSKfV3BGQfHhHu0f82aeQCGABxK1XyfO9KTQunZkxX-kHQjaT7EsTCyEOKzj6IbcNF-pS4MtrPZ2gHZuRBccDJwoT-bq5wjzI=> .

Ericsson: Phones Getting Smarter

 

Yesterday, mobile networking company Ericsson released new data and projections on mobile penetration worldwide. Today, the company says smartphones are 25-30% of all mobile phone plans, but account for 55% of mobile phones sold in Q3 2013. Furthermore, mobile subsciptions "are expected to reach 9.3 billion by 2019, and more than 60 percent of these -- 5.6 billion -- will be for smartphones." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197HZcBUi_ARLhceboq6AkxXqc_wjKcdfbxsk5uQyGjvkRESgMzbiusJZ-3QzUALoWOXlN_KOtzrjhW2vxnVCsHySiEopVk0y2-P2zT2HINoQ0Iz20v-GyybhTJPxnDSiK6Qo8z6zdtVjti5nsIK7x6jbisYZD3lHRgpGy8VwWKCnJGMLb1_be2C2JU8knQ38> .

 

The Wild West Of Mobile Ads

 

Business Insider reports that from its Ignition Conference, mobile advertising realities were front and center as Criteo prez Greg Colement suggested that mobile ads might or might not suck (we're not paraphrasing). Also, The Weather Company CRO Curt Hecht said that when his company attempted programmatic buying and selling through mobile ad exchanges, it was hard to know who was who. Hecht stated, "It felt like the Wild West. We had people coming in saying they were only a data company and then a week later, they were a network." My mother, my sister. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197HZcBUi_ARPQO52kW0zr82xlBDdc1gQH9cQDJ7X1Uv8n-40YdmelX5BpIMem-l-vzvdM3wkyYc69FzxY1vQG2Bv8SosrFKFZPaMSc_OeYQk2uwnGTceVb8Ghyg06ZXHKsq5GLaEVOmJ83bnilK8MqnmG3xUHOn5aJ3yi4_uvSMdel3E6xA5ANS5ayPOV0NgRS6MTGjMQrw=> .

 

Editorial Convergence

 

Editorial and ecommerce are converging, and Thrillist Media Group (TMG) is the latest to take advantage of the trend, MediaPost reports. The new feature is called "Shops" and it will put product information directly into editorial. "Of course, there is [editorial sensitivity] when you combine content and commerce and we think about that a lot ... but innovative companies find ways to make it work," said Ben Lerer, co-founder and CEO of TMG. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197HZcBUi_ATtBrMzb-tVGNOkNZEyFrXDTPd9mtQ0cH7a0LgqpBfGOihFqK7Mn6uDZQiRmrTmv0R22M-aeX7C26_Tsc3P98-CIjnJVvvcmorFW2U98gFCiaZXVFmeR3ww9bX0Sm_bUyBLYlyFB2DZLRVHw3I6gOcjCLPzxvESNv-Oxvh70adJQBLLTDr80b4VZmAf4naAyh-j5M0h3qGfiR3wNtK-pHegPHf3Q1sGKvI=> . Thrillist, Vox, Gawker and Business Insider are all part of a new wave of "digital native" publishing, reports Reuters' Felix Salmon <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197HZcBUi_ARoHvagW5THtwi8ODnQMeFyqyHo918cFK15pAZun92CAjlrz7SbXq93p2c0FfqMS8HZtls3X0mGcQt4m5-5S8oFxYXmShPlaLXCDCVrDiDeUUudFnrRFFBnCsK6KFEZCgytOrIHHOiIOPatxX3EucJh3xZ83_l-ijTpEudqOaEIYmLwtQTaIyZKHsXr-Mkwp8TLtd8emo7qdw==> .

 

Video Traffic

 

When it comes to online video, Netflix and YouTube are leading the pack in the US, according to data from Sandvine. Interestingly, Amazon and Hulu account for very little peak downstream traffic, as GigaOM points out. YouTube is the dominant force in all of the regions sampled, which included parts of Europe and Latin America. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197HZcBUi_ASmolvqTV6obkE2eFDICWdCE0_psPgl4J68fWrJKdsVJ9HRBsptSseGPfM1aLzV-meK0-etl_SoDbLD4NL6zev2FV2IUvRkADyNCVOU2dTs_OlAcmvTkDsGswwwYriAkXaEZ2kAztA9er7zkCskTXbJmgv428BHrAuR4Ca7lLGKmK3KNcIhEAie> .

 

Stock Market Stuff

 

In Ad Age, Alex Kantrowitz reviews the plunge of ad-tech companies' stock in the public markets when Tremor reported less-than-stellar earnings late last week. Pivotal Research analyst Brian Wieser tells Kantrowitz, "So far most investors have not paid particular mind to competitive issues that will inevitably come to bear on those [ad-tech] companies which have recently gone public. So it is safe to say that valuations have not reflected these factors to date." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197HZcBUi_ASMw4or9TspKUg8RqGPNhrbPfu7CDsGOaJq4ebuBE-BHLhgven7g_PHbOuLgu4Q70-AZQh6lHC-JGvWyhUFQi1R-NH4gjmL8951qoFhhL9kUPwJACYb82_9zlFvdM56VLbwOAql8ELrYMokb1k48k5Azsq8l2cY8NMCI2AwWIa9ZdzV4_CPxeaS> .

Marketing Report Card

 

IgnitionOne released a new, in-house progress report -- "2013 Integrated Marketing Survey" -- that examines digital marketing efforts. "Moving away from complexity and toward simplicity is something that all marketers strive for, but aren't all actually doing," said Will Margiloff, IgnitionOne's CEO. "This report further highlights the need for marketers to break down the silos within their organization and the challenges that they face in centralizing and integrating their digital efforts." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197HZcBUi_ASAeP9I2NvXiFf4W39TKxO_deJIADqnp-cx6On8JlH17ZJh-2ChMrHKm6eJ7v0E6sxedya0rX-DtY9uMIQZR36lleAyzfdH6kOylpi1DLn78XtTWMyp0p7J68nlCM6c3MvPXIJEiow8Fc4bextqrsDvp_TEPudW0kFrzYXRVJciYgq5WnNLZ74IfzYGnLfwpTNQp09Bfq2dEpLO7DFWoGUTZgNRiKWIhZA=> . And, get the report (pay with PII and first born) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197HZcBUi_ASWG_nNz4pdvcF9gJd27vgeJnwO_kkscU7ndIuJeMFXJIpdKB22FGMz7x4ppUoWr_cYvVjsqhUDUqovH3gbDPh6mjWpvJypSqf3-N4CvJG3joIIj8cOjqYrptYQecA9p2-0pPEMv5nPzlyQAY8j5GIyeFVjef7IneeT_Q6pMWMqVNwREoEgx0N-hmN1krBCgl0=> .

PubMatic Responds

 

In a blog post on Friday, sell-side platform PubMatic responded to critical comments made by AppNexus CEO Brian O'Kelley in an AdExchanger interview last week <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjKuw85sbKxozhh2dxmOiuO1OVCiqMABqeh24IwcUYDvCNERFbJWihj7SZAhXW7drLiNNl6cqKpZDeupCrbLfUV_D44zd1m8mgBLetdyKXkIBpvCyHSxSeVJpN9IzwA0-BesXAjdE4gVEMbQOfnR4S6x0yzskjVqx8dPdLXwO4vZVuMKkI7vczsoPRbUEPmq2Jjwdfary79lxA==> . The blog states, "We respect the business that Brian has built in display, but his comments were troubling. He basically told publishers to drop dead, declaring them irrelevant and not offering them any real capabilities. We take publisher needs seriously..." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjISYn8Ntc7cvtXr7M5THJ4CtvAa05su3Qsyc7ojNxUN7At3ayMjKMh_AqedF24yDxKOtVVfoO9juCpIWMWFvdwniwFR6ReWmqA02_0j4x5pa1_KfKINPEUth7tr6vXWKOGqhT-tWLSDfX9WRVFGf0AQ8jktxOcqfLc=> .

 

Real-Time Inflation Index

 

Founding CEO of Metamarkets, David Soloff, has turned his attention to his new company, Premise, and in a New York Times feature article he takes the wraps of his stealthy enterprise. The NYT explains "the premise", "By analyzing the photos of prices and the placement of everyday items like piles of tomatoes and bottles of shampoo and matching that to other data, Premise is building a real-time inflation index to sell to companies and Wall Street traders, who are hungry for insightful data." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjIj6QId5PE-9mxwewPfmZj5j8UGRtTz-B8kBYnD8B04YbX0zG45sVNbnz5ClfafGz9hRD122W9PDpFcu97PqsTLpr450ilHYMlF1K2gLhx6hPLkQT0TP6lUCGkb6993vnuZ3VE1nU97gdzss4_P9sNt6a7M3811ypDZTSiMkR7m1UZt74TAPmjzJr98fv-vifbMWY4sRYJxmPhXrrnb-_yUBTiQ175333tOUUFwURZpwpd7tUO6O-99> . Big data gets bigger.

 

Programmatic And The CMO

 

In an article in the UK's MarketingWeek, reporter Ronan Shields says recent agreement over brand safety standards <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjJYTr_rjglLgC9wzelKJ2-pFs-jlCKXMH07vvplLhZp2vIkiAPh5R_FtrZDnEFONC3PHj5Dn9VCrkKagid23W6NfKBgJ1erS-T69iBsoIii-cXXzQnVgFCrh5EINUVWW9camJRQ5NDDsMW-wPMH0Uc_gVHb87akUbNN5LOUhti4XkzL04PZN1E1VDHiHQ7xq1qa6gYdwf8eZQ==>  for display media in the UK won't make programmatic media any better for brand marketers. He writes, "I think high-profile scares in recent history will further stall ad budgets from going programmatic. For instance, the technical jargon of content verification tools may be music to the ears of a media agency's head of digital trading, but how can they sell this in to CMOs when the memories of high-profile brands' ads appearing against obscene content linger[?]" Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjK9l-TM1PSg-bfT_ZCbuNHUokvaHJaCqvrNjzmdftKh3IO2A1Xh_53fd6IU8_vp_OV2P4s-65zRvpvnNjScG_NERa-xjfcY6RDqxW9xj-yWZjIwl-sBXzAU29CHlIMXsthRrgN-JfYlHlYFbAmw9m62cNz7fYoHt0ooJ1bwGqekL1nRnF_R8rX_eoKX9w7WJMdeJ0nX3GzH_3xGgU57O3_M9B9XwNK1kO9WzqKc2FtKMw==> .

 

The Prada Private Exchange

 

From TVN's Future of Video Upfront in Sydney last week, AdNews' Brandon Coyne reports panelist observations on programmatic media momentum: "Private exchanges are like a Prada store where only discerning customers are invited and there is no question of anything but a fixed price. Meanwhile private marketplaces are like boutique stores that stock a range of luxury brands." Private exchanges have picked up speed. Read more on TV-online convergence, too <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjIQZIOICfApjqG0xnXDAx8_3YBLdmN1Dx6Z2CXyM6rb3JUic72fqfxgebPXqd951XnWDn31-bbULarZGIAz2TbbLpvBQ_a8WkpyymO9butNp85LF_qA9FD7XQsiiysnX0vlKpmPzB9OfCu8hW692sMuldg-uEBY9bWMiA77_ofqxA==> .

 

Targeting Waste

 

Advertisers have more than bots to worry about, cautions Chen Wang, IRI's principal for new media solutions -- they should also think about their poor targeting. He told Adweek's Mike Shields, "Marketers are wasting valuable media dollars on consumer segments unlikely to yield an acceptable return." Wang found that some online advertisers waste half of their efforts on consumers who are not at all interested in their product. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjJYJtmar2X_ddmvY3EDROqwYqYYJbBpX4dMEV7ockDo2Cyw29ct-EkWWB9Iw5N58RERrU_WlcAYDakbQieqxRGgKOUE_922mbIrrWeEdOQ95MWhapIBAQ0K_zr6egMOD-XPjyWkltUfjD2UyOdGUgmpwWmC5D-qp-qH4F8YjcBjOSsnhyBpZtdWuSe0gcREacPRmmk3hJqElfmrbS-Z_b2n> .

Storytelling Roll-Up

 

According to The New York Times, Vox Media will announce today that it's buying the local-blog-with-attitude network Curbed for between $20 million and $30 million. Vox CEO Jim Bankoff tells the NYT "that the Curbed brands were a smart addition because they coveted the same kind of reader."  He added, "Both Vox and Curbed value storytelling and as a result have attracted the otherwise hard to reach young, affluent, social consumers. We think this combined expanded platform will clearly attract premium advertisers." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjJBx6ch1YwnviHAM2rK2ZDuxFNe2qQbXtUsSYkSLSuHBS6ZCNQUg-oa7B32D9Kk5g55CWXd2j-zSxCP-KndzhgB4QzLXxgJ20oNEK09Gv2pSZv5knYA6ueTIIf5Ato-RTjE9IXhzOJGGFcH7CeqCRHQYaQnWPD6goBjQ2QNZ5diAaNi8WD0icgvQM6mY0SCf4May5NxiYyWPCcjG6WwF0Xj4ipMLAYvD2I=> .

 

Attributing Online Offline

 

Commenting on new comScore data <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjLhyANtd8MTs-vWWyTkWqlXzZ8fYIqL2M4e5GxURSRsNHT4r_f14XfFpaihAO7pXY2_OSVGb-TnXH6NK_C4qoSMrKSV_eQKVxT2q4b07I1egcLGDAcXAFyXLECgZhhZzSowCER45I7C0qX2N6KKyry4JdkQKqHSlW8O0-zDaiqsfC006r4NDuJ7H47WJ31CtB1cdjJKG07sRTo4UEgOQqL1j455WxZtGimOH0c-Ne2LpNdZkQQzUoppN7s7nRTshy_jYAdPy-bQ0RFjGC0Tmzhhq4aJlpYsq5-HE7nucAI5slglGNwuBLdUg4cAd97LYp0=>  showing US desktop-based ecommerce has grown 13% in the last year to $47.5 billion, analyst Greg Sterling notes on his blog, "Once again, as people are getting very excited about these numbers, I feel compelled to point out that this remains a fraction of local sales and Internet-influenced offline buying. The overwhelming use of smartphones in stores (60% to 80%) and multiscreen shopping means that the consumer path to purchase this holiday season will be more 'considered' and convoluted than ever. However it doesn't change the fact that most buying will still take place locally, in stores." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjK_5GflU3DaoswjXTY-FmrWxW5wXZvTYpOfPufpxytWt48NAU2H9azNTyyXXmcqIhXecr3640n4NujZ5sqRnjw-bd1HtucJ51yljCajU0BqIySRVSaUHGn6rmyhE6WgoiPJaS9syZzd5xNx0qMZDl6hvhDqb0ZJorB1er92iLppRph6NIHX4m0HCDmKE5FAnDLFOwZk3yZ4hJEt4X4iNTIL3-alutQjNos=> .

 

Getting More Mobile

 

WPP has made an acquisition of the mobile variety, scooping up brand app builder Bottle Rocket. According to the press release, the company's unaudited revenue for the past 12 months was $17 million, and they work with clients such as Scripps, National Geographic and NBC Universal. WPP acquired a minority stake in another mobile company in August, Mutual Mobile Inc., as agencies scramble to stay in front of client demand for effective mobile solutions. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CLuDW8KlkjLfp5K24mGV7oGWwiRVE-xIEEikiXl5XWDTZqwd1o4MMgmxpxBcmYoV2M-DMQxszXY6XgoiRz7dhcZW7NEAlhPjs4byQnlDPZSXluJkxqdT3cipCwAZqvOcAEfMibUYZMjf0oRSo7-zZqcMh-I-Q7xJ2BeJzBe67IFaC9LmUUmeKl7PXomskbkra4k1dqo3ddkCIzyrwv2URjQbDB6j_ONV> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>

eBay's Programmatic Success

 

Programmatic is becoming a big part of the display pie for eBay, who says the volume of ad impressions on its exchange has grown fivefold, UK-based The Drum reported. "The budgets currently being allocated to private marketplaces are much smaller than for open but that's changing fast. I expect our private marketplace will more than double in terms of business we do through it next year," said Guy Jones, head of programmatic trading at eBay. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UHlSFO75NMgFgB5a1xrX9CQM9X9G4DzonY_UW5bp6YXC6gGiyu4xqVJy7bse-bXPSGjVFQ_zvXinVtjoUSajx04WgopYW2xVIEdMA9YiuVTxEMSzb8013AVVbMgCatOA3UF6JzUniawRiwR5aRuKYP7bNAWkkAZlSkmO1_-WF4uUEIr9NJyzfO2_UtmSG9rTvXjdO7aDgv6vrO9KYuX0wzjsQY_c4CtlISwl5pwTVqh1xbYayPxOQw==> .

 

Nielsen OCR In The Wild

 

Adweek's Mike Shields notes that some buy-side clients are using Nielsen Online Campaign Ratings (OCR) data to effect media buys through the Google platform. He adds, "The company isn't saying which brands are involved just yet. But the hope is to test and learn, and eventually make the OCR option available to all Google video advertisers. ComScore's VCE is in the mix as well." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UHlSFO75NMgpt6xDPLiAmvZPjaAxDGH8JPG_KQVb0A7z6YTnU9BoMgEbKeQh86YC3ksiotUvxZzPu-SBq8XaYV9UyWz-GlsOiZKDsLsyz7VvVT6USQFSJQOt-pc8kFdVMgwPy5N_CLAJlEZKl8JHGF0cERxd5p50LQWD4h0Y5eMSMNNquTfnx2yPaB5HlaU2QWANLSz4rOVg7e7lmUBzVw==> 

 

Programmatic Worldwide

 

Programmatic is changing the media agency model, TubeMogul VP of Ops Daniel Schotland told Australia's AdNews. The market is very similar to the US, says Schotland, who adds, "Over the next few years 'you could start to see [Australian media agencies] struggle to do business the way they are doing it today. They will need to explore other avenues. It could be a programmatic-or-bust situation.'" Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UHlSFO75NMgfiYkYyGx4AZMxMwaKGnpaK0TLZy3Y8laQFLdnyBefDljNv-qwN1f7rTdpcHHjM0nDzcI_irTNVxItTDdOM1eVKLArfoVz5JmcPT1Qi5KDs8Y2Sp3qXcNyrxRmEVh2mr4JowOiGp4R8Eqhfma5acIiTG_H5XNOIXMaHzDPOUSW9w==> .

 

Targeting Stars

 

TechCrunch received a "hot" tip that Facebook is testing a star rating system for Pages on the desktop version of the site, which gives users more sentiment than just a simple "like." As the article's author, Darrell Etherington, points out, likes are used to express everything from interest to disapproval, so it's hard to tell exactly what a like means. Although nothing has been officially confirmed, this potential system could give Facebook an edge when competing with rating services such as Yelp. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UHlSFO75NMgUQOdK6KK9LTQ5WzTagk1DoeZoSZ_MvWCg3xZ2cMtCTbLedMvKi9RT0yU_IL2reyQQqjXO5Pe4PTJ36mm0qwIPMR4Kf0occO_FpM0ULqyDbv_shZxpENdeRsVnbfL4h37LZ_Q12pH7fJPOHOyCdyokPMtRFrTKIBiY5w71FVoHeQ==> . Could be another targeting attribute for ads, too.

 

Incumbents Vs. Insurgents

 

Digital is changing marketing for enterprise companies and continually pushing companies to adopt new technologies, as pointed out by the Thomvest team in a comprehensive report on the space. But who can win at ad tech amidst the vast startup landscape? The Thomvest team offers, "There is a clear opportunity for those companies that have already reached scale (such as a number of companies that are recently public or at a stage where this is an option) to try to compete with the incumbents head on." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UHlSFO75NMgkaX_zEqCVYt1zAdlJBAw20sPu7-W_E4S0MqgMOVmBjX6iP6YUbbbNfoHlPhlrGMk3kxc0Ekh3YvoMAa1gluNPnWYPBm0Ks4ebI1XWASVa-jm5Db2aSzlm0Rg752YrcN6L7b_5TjLvmnSa35z_Wzv5_kOrCrtI0Og=> .

App Retention Bonus

 

Appboy wants to be the "ExactTarget for Mobile Apps," and has secured $7.6 million from IDG Ventures and Buddy Media CEO Mike Lazerow to get there. The money will help build out loyalty and retention efforts on behalf of developers. "The platform automatically generates robust user profiles and empowers app marketers to further engage their audience with a suite of marketing automation products." Clients include Urban Outfitters, GSN, Bloomberg, Shape and PopSci. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fxKNgNBvg1jN3Gck7lBE6VCNvwI4MQjJ0v5rYl6ATcDAgdlz7CK5ab5C_v9VwWaByIUZjddyzO5jR3iLjd82G_vLsWMo-q2SvYUCSJBN1O7YB91Fs6nLuC6OMFokAp4s9_PQWQDUkdH5H228jHT_E9wfr7Vc6wrdZyUAxw_imxDNCnDoHeF2_-dshf4-iofTrgyinArMGSbZ3B_2p94jK-HOtBi4BvuXTnd56Hv7xreQhRyO6FL7IQ==> 

 

Mobile Yield For The Masses

 

PubMatic's mobile SDK is no longer for "premium" publishers only. A new self-serve version can be leveraged by anyone, potentially bringing new long-tail mobile supply to the PubMatic marketplace. Meanwhile small publishers will get exposure to more demand. "We are working to fulfill the promise of one platform solution by offering a self-service version of PubMatic's premium platform to the next generation of publishers," said President Kirk McDonald. Mobile publishers that bring 30 million-plus impressions are automatically upgraded to "full service." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fxKNgNBvg1gzijMXjH1s2okp3C9dBtI778KOF7oo2BYPvpohwfUrjPWaIZTHczd_UtpTguyR7TdZJ_218i6pw8BoUn_SeRHHH01QHP3XcBudW6qcHqrMDToKKCVZ10qyjs91fDaY5r8aOfj9J_rJm1W627-4NXxc0SKw5s0kllE8QzOvmpBQ1VdhHwTm3NkXp4T8eH7gt1-f4YvyAcDQZQ==> .

 

Photosharing Contender

 

Israel-based Instagram competitor Mobli closed a $60 million round led by América Móvil, according to VentureBeat's Tom Cheredar. Although it's not the only company doing photo and video sharing, the company does have a lot of investor and celebrity backing. The company has raised $88 million in all. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fxKNgNBvg1i4Hd--9YuOLB_t7NA9QPachc6KcSf44i9geB-AZbvVC44TwLZruwA2SZbxMxTttqLklQVUQ6_Q9I48QaVGrv_LvdYRwWN66CSgFNHi38lhGc0P8K7gEYOThO2LFk4dLBcwF52fr21i0do57vRHrXF0> .

 

Catalog-ic Converters

 

Convertro is adding support for catalog data to its attribution platform. The company said a big retailer is using the solution "to link its direct mail efforts (for example, catalog) with its online marketing initiatives (for example, email) at the user level." Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fxKNgNBvg1jdA9gg55mmMTjk-WzNtXU2jlUkkqhbROFnSbWw_5ujJlT1BS5Db-ZN4PPotlD_F1xab_oJ5TXW6tCH4N1vYpGbvF_5yOtaMdPASYswL-XkC5-SLqXmZ3U_LTn7dIjASlET-18sjPiHQkjE6ZzEyEFbx17LPprIwj3LvjzATB_NLVZcKK5DaMVucymH0saIhAWu7tUljov7QW84_ZXHj6ogn6V8_p7nKX5LDKYTCoZPYEKu37T1A89X> 

 

ReGlued

 

After an earlier deal to sell itself to Viggle fell apart, social TV startup GetGlue has found a new buyer in i.TV, Ad Age reports. Both companies are private so no financial information was disclosed, but GetGlue has about 1.2 million active monthly users. Although it's a small group who are highly active on social media. i.TV founder Brad Pelo tells Simon Dumenco, "While we're very interested in growing the GetGlue base, we also want to be true to what the base is intended to be, which is sort of a superfan community, and that isn't everybody." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fxKNgNBvg1gUVxFgI9spxHFnkcZu1OOliiSxO93e9j8q5Sn1bEsUA9AEWamCi4N9AAyx248-3sW8v7DkD1pem_IxHTvKmQ4BlTT_mFPyB0XRre5me5bEd2u77bBFYYcQhrIU9px2ooej9LFYBSw6ob-4yj-mx5xvlPGgUtI0svalVd-E2yowzs90nqiyecUbJjPxbInfyNJvgwxLXKRwEC-WV8hw9_ZEjKn66gxb8glBDe7N5twBjw==> .

Measuring Time

 

WebSpectator, an advertising exchange that measures the amount of time people spend viewing an ad in real time, launched its new "guaranteed to see" metric yesterday at ad:tech New York. By placing a line of code on webpages, the company claims it can measure the time spent viewing an ad down to the millisecond. "Finally, advertisers can buy what's real and eliminate waste," WebSpectator CEO Andre Parreira told AdExchanger. The company reached $12 million in revenue within six months and has about 500 customers, according to Parreira, who has set a goal to hit $100 million by the end of 2014. "This is a money-making machine," he claimed. Read the press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fxKNgNBvg1iF1h78ObnunuFZaoZUUZMOD9E5yvKdeSWgh-PysjRTLZMmdJEwEJmpyWm8Oeel5QVzln80WlakSxBSN-Nt5uckSO_SkJ4LjWn5L-MtWtuxEJZ5KYxlBc1fXwpNjIkD3XsP4zGTVmoEcB-uFVRlJ569Uki57JHyPJ5kHgBcnDUEyVpego3ztioskp5gJV_xPQDtpO8VtwBkfg==>

DAA Transparency Survey

 

The Digital Advertising Alliance (DAA) recently polled approximately 1,000 US adults about their thoughts on ad transparency. More than 57% of respondents said they wouldn't visit any of the free, ad-supported sites that they currently use if those sites converted to pay models. And 51.3% said they'd be more likely to click on an online ad that included an icon that allowed them to opt out of ad-related information collection. "Americans expect ads to provide them with transparency and choice, and are more likely to do business with advertisers that provide it," said DAA Managing Director Lou Mastria in a statement. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLEnLMsr7OuN6q1oCb3ez9tpIXcA_cD2QpNZUZC0bVwv7Mu-Ro0TYtnMFfRU6LTZaBi2G1gYtPAbXcBNkKXjAGrWbs2ELUQHJYvBwyGrGuv828QWw8owIZCsvfRipeOXV6knbc-T7fZuRhfqLh-uHEKbEU7oUC-IGzP5cpJ3YOSBtTB9Aowoea08Y1q508cKatUYiSgrbDrIbNaOgKXStfDX> 

 

Success Cards

 

Webtrends took advantage of Twitter's lead-generation cards and built a socialcentric campaign to promote its product to marketing professionals. The company employed a number of different methods for figuring out which keywords and users to target, and saw a 500% decrease in cost per lead and a 300% decrease in cost per engagement. "Previously, Twitter was just an awareness mechanism for our marketing team. Now it's the focal point of all our social lead-generation initiatives, especially when it comes to net new name acquisition," said John Lee, manager for brand and social marketing at Webtrends. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLEg5bJv1DGgXZE8FwS4u0ChZFH3qKkKaKJNdVZPUKqWbhhbMzVinYBg_uNZHUajHYtA6Mx9KUU-7SZROp1bFAXN-Dl4R2X1WTsFmnVE7YLPj2BzRbX7DzSHUwCmJo3yuhACEYObEi4k5qVzgUHYB-jg> .

 

The Native Ad Wagon

 

The Associated Press is the latest publisher to jump on the native advertising wagon, Digiday's Josh Sternberg reports. The sponsored content will be text, video and photography, and will only run on the AP's site, not on those of its syndicates. "We're not trying to make people think this is something AP produced," said Ken Detlet, the AP's VP of digital advertising strategy and sales. "They'll know it's something the brand is bringing to the table." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLFnbHkRPzbL0fVn-CqqNsJYoQKC024R05GglBcg0iu9NdnvevKghqbUOG3DjM5vefwcaoOc_hz9aWcMiptiGcX1Q9JDeXkJ0WJeW5vDc2Gd02w9yqLgTEI_R-Q7CGazu_t5wGTZ8WjCbRFMK2puCUJ6aBzIQZ3dXiA=> .

 

Boom Or Bust

 

Depending on whom you ask, ad tech is either in a golden era or peaking. A paper written by Tim Hwang and Adi Kamdar of the Nesson Center for Internet Geophysics paints a really grim picture for digital advertising's future, but Doug Weaver, founder and CEO of Upstream, vehemently disagrees with their predictions. The penmen of the working paper see advertising as a commodity market, but Weaver feels advertising is "a thousand different models across a dozen channels." Read the blog post here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLGWM995rICJmbspXxLMw7dwO4Eykz8aKrPgVWPQf6MTsaOITvUTYr7T_kZcAFqEdVFpLLBjJsm0hmunJi90KdmkjunsJ5tCdEB09SIxGSaxodxJevLMRaQ_u_94YUSmgrQ=> .

 

Picture Of Success

 

There has been a lot of talk about Instagram ads since the company was bought by Facebook last year, and after the company's first sponsored post, the results point to a promising future. Analytics company Nitrogram said an ad brought Michael Kors more than 33,000 new followers, and it generated 370% more likes than the average of the company's last five nonpromoted posts. Not all users were thrilled however, as 20% of comments on the ad were negative in nature. Read the report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLEKgnMdqyRTam3iVNY9wu2CwRlLJ2TCsEuzOuKYYq9Gnfym9BO9zaxffybcPiJSa6bf9dvL4ZRUiQKu1PLUAeFxNOmX_HoiXDVRG8W9V2X5kDI8b6WuhdEkl0Kqe4YMG75DTyhYdQNTzkAspKM8t4HxAsge4GtpI5k=> .
