VP Of Programmatic

 

Of all the types of companies in advertising, it seems weather is the ideal candidate for the real-time nature of programmatic advertising. That could be a good reason why The Weather Channel has created the role of VP for programmatic and given it to Jeremy Hlavacek, formerly VP of operations and strategic partnerships for WeatherFX. He will report to Jeremy Steinberg, SVP, digital ad sales, who said, "Programmatic buying is already a rapidly growing revenue channel for The Weather Company, and we know under Jeremy's leadership of our programmatic efforts we'll see even more impressive growth." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLGG0dqeE0yPsqIC12rO9xSGGVrXZdsMkyXjFNuvfSO9qNb-JJvpKhQJPPLbTm5bywI2rHsFRojqEqnozUV3uiQ4hfx0U64fY-lAKE9gSaJA0h1VxvlZ0mHAG-gXeXA7ixhWzEya3dupHSnQQW_uy0UeNW3hxuEMh7V9lTfPoLK2dQ==> .

 

Cookie Jar Not Empty

 

Third-party cookies are in limbo right now, but 47% of impressions measured in AdMonsters' Index Quarterly Cookie Report are cookies matched to third-party data. Only 17% of impressions have no cookie at all, suggesting the little bites of code are still vital despite the surge in negative press. Privacy issues aside, mobile is really driving a shift away from cookies, as AdMonsters found 41% of mobile impressions were not cookied. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLHevXwuExXh1SkwCqOobTe6b007u3YPhwTxXlmZj5Rn92fQ7nXWsP-ygvdYqZHKbFOeRRJFGiVk5xCN5QySEQOBdU6OhU_0LOhXO3f34NZZXNjQX5MMYSzLCYxTM8rE6dxCBxKr8eCVzfOPQnnTAQbi> .

 

Programmatic And The Agency

 

Not everyone is heralding the arrival of programmatic, as Adweek's Sam Thielman points out, there are still some groups, such as TV buyers, who don't care for automation. Thielman spoke to the Rubicon Project's Jay Sears, who gave a little more insight into programmatic and the agency role in its future, saying, "We're quite certain automation will touch every corner of advertising. If you want to see the way the world is going, you need to be studying the display market, the mobile market and, after those two, the video market." Touch more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLEmEuFv1lEt4HzTKysXFFx4RWvp1Oy29mTZp0OIPI7-jdWLQnXNzGxJXsmis6ymV9ODaPEyWEs4-rg1E-BwUB8wdz3Nk_Bug67PF2F4_68JrhDKDnFLSZf5CTz1qAROrclAe-KsepWJ1XF7r3lfyVOxpURjvwqFstdLg9BAIljd5oRUytzp1HdGSI0cjN6VK8QX4RowWj3HepsPLBG3DVTd> .

 

Pay Fast

 

J. Crew is joining MasterCard's MasterPass program, which streamlines the checkout process for consumers. MasterCard is joining the likes of companies such as PayPal, Amazon and Google, among others, who are trying to make headway in the digital payment space. Mobile Commerce Daily's Rebecca Borison points out that as consumers gear up for the holiday season, they may be looking for ways to get shopping done more quickly, the perfect opportunity for something like this to take off. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rpiYJ7x4MLF9QujMLx6Iuut21JR9rk52mV8wrtHdwUXNKqsiHBxiTGVPTnrm_CpV1PAUUHERqGS2f7JkCXLIKtV83-r_DvtB3C4xFV-tACCBmAccI9VNDFR9nayN2Ob0ENfWr1q-vYatPdCDlp6lF1vRIIoFIeqg3rN-7LEHpIMGA17kj9It25Q4MxU6L4qKR-Df1o_O_3TzwofxeQ51Xb3Lt_S0X2_g> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?

Tesco's Ad Screens

 

There was a time when scanning technology for the purposes of ad serving would have seemed invasive, but GigaOM's David Meyer points out that's no longer the case. Tesco is taking advantage of OptimEyes' technology by installing ad screens that also have a camera for scanning customers nearby, and then serving them demographically appropriate ads. The company says no personal information is collected and no photos or video are taken or stored, so Meyer says this is not one for the privacy advocates to get worked up about. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSBTOfFh_MS9_5ZJC3vuy_x42ASov4i5Y5qDFxab_GasBvGsTGsoA0ZJkUSdu1pfGXHZ7Nu8irEi-TlPs9n9y2iHuxBgkFvDk0ec9Ni86JkrzerO6qEqha3e0WJm77sjlNhq9FoGBOc5UAbTfKBKHcoGn7G0JNoNmCT6uH4GXVdyDPZx7qWq2VXyoHw1gMlwIq1gs3-T9rsCaFPuAYokhBHF> .

 

Visible Measures App Ads

 

Visible Measures has a video-app ad network of sorts, according to PandoDaily, which details the VM's content network plans. The app network delivers algo-influenced content through Samsung smart TVs: "[Visible Measures] makes its money by helping content creators find more viewers for their video. One of its lead products is Contagion, a predictive modeling tool that lets publishers see, with a claimed 90% accuracy, how much money they need to spend and legwork they need to do in order to reach a certain number of viewers." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSBi0g6V1UphEIqD1Z2GyNoS9kU-lQJ5zmwekBx5rf6AuJE9nXS8q-hfiXUvLfRT3wQgIwQr2GBnVbS7ueqr3gJY7bs56XBNrgVruP2gROLPpqLeQxu-jajIKD8M8u9P27z_cOoCRYst-eYecpX_had-DgmDPMV385W4OlBlesRCLravnIlMngOY93aP5KSqOZXzXsqcOY2KUjrYXHf6urU6vG0fwQ90lOk=> .

 

Data Success

 

In a sign of the times, Lotame is reporting record success and expansion as data-driven marketing becomes mainstream. "It has been a huge year not only for Lotame but for the DMP and ad-tech space as a whole," said Andy Monfried, founder and CEO of Lotame. "The surge in DMP adoption is evidence that publishers and marketers on a global scale are realizing the impact that leveraging Big Data and an audience-driven approach can deliver in terms of revenue, efficiency and performance." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSB7mY3WtU1kU3GPVWZnoygDNEvLLt4fFxd3XKZX9wFjarMT6VAsIcVIEaPNG21AAR2fi8ycQzvK6jhcaVFEOnHN9ADtJLZaL_xBej5lUrMyOywEa54Qfh4kXJVUqQDttRH-lnZl7Y3xPI2BjNNW9g5WgWi_OpmkOqtdfFiLSwsUODEVTvAufjcFupaXmQAjrAH5PIV898P1PoDu-Z93AHNlg3-k9wXqWEH0uoma6Ik-aWcK4zzLe-4zOIRVLimZtqDuZHebubxiYYCIx3oPaegrW-iuv1UfbiM=> .

 

Programmatic Publishing

 

An IAB and Winterberry Group study <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSBR6TtDjD8eu7i6xdmALmcEiyi3JLZpkVR2CjAPaSjcdPlT6xu3oJQBBtgqGTOl6EGVQPZiUEW5XvyB9T2oRKZOXnczJqYP-Y2K8q5NSLrJRBf-ItJftc5Li__El2Cp-9s=>  found that 85% of advertisers and 72% of publishers are using programmatic auction strategies. That number is expected to grow as advertisers and publishers get more comfortable with the concept of programmatic, but there are still hurdles to overcome with brand safety. "The rise of programmatic buying and the inherent operational efficiencies it promises offers a positive sea change for the entire digital industry," said Patrick Dolan, EVP and COO for IAB. "But, if we're going to take full advantage of programmatic's buying's [sic] potential, it is incumbent upon the industry to overcome barriers to its success." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSB2ipn8JpS7YPYMfXFNHI4Oz2mpSxGZdFIR_vtSOCPGZtv0NPdG988ir8jaKXG-0HIJUx-H1w-sB8uXUMVP6Zxej8mkGal7ETnOjJVWYcnw7pvRAx6vQxGZMT8jwVI0g4J7kGMZoYnWOXL7iYXa0YelTPJNzhS17eI0KdNWcMHDsrvxScVkkhmvHJ2UTsuTD9IRf8E1x3RY3Qzd1E5YZo5bJMzG5u57r98=> .

 

Evolving TV

 

A new trend has emerged in television, called delayed viewing (it's like time-shifting's brother), and it's changing the way networks and advertisers think about the medium. The New York Times' Bill Carter points out that networks only get paid for up to three days of a show being viewed, due to the emergence of digital recording technology, but that will soon be extended to seven days. "These are our viewers," said Kevin Reilly, chairman of entertainment for the Fox Broadcasting Company. "It's not as though they are lesser viewers or negligible viewers." The next step for networks will be tackling streaming video online, which currently isn't rated or measured. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSA2_Heah4-w3GdMf9NqvYi22iavc1oPNmjTiKtSxvqU3QN8So82N5GAOOWn6cxcRjJXG8Zhil676OBFljoD0MRNZuHeTXSTl3DTHspn_19LMO7kbFW1SOtfUQbNZArizqr-zCSF6aBB0JgxKc9Ko_f6Rg4EH1Mc_Kdst1p9c7ok1Dl3was0Z0q05EW9yM2sr55IOv_jjSs0AUmzF2X4gLNk7hfvKQk63M_oR5W3-5NugPWyl2JrUs3cnOmQeq-Lk8GSSpu1Do_axd31Ysa1XNbSRMzDdqlZ1K4=> .

Programmatic Dictionary

 

Many attempts are being made to define programmatic, but there's still a lot of confusion in the advertising community. Adweek's Mike Shields has put together a seven-page primer, attempting to explain what is currently known as "programmatic." He concludes that there's no clear consensus yet. But the two things that everyone seems to agree on is that programmatic is only going to get bigger, and it's here to stay. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSCei66RtMXTYTBQmFCyOaLaw91RpsJhfLCPDnc6gYBmssSxAaJ-gqUYJwdT_rEPIDKuQVVbyKW1XAc1_n4xVYRTTrNXpZ5_6jrf_GAL1ec0jUvqU8vVBaHHaIDm0Lr5h17-Kq7UdrbsSYekdvvkApO_mn2-yngLWtOMOJTHsYPnMA==> .

 

RPTV

 

Revenue Per Timeline View (RPTV). The New York Times' Mark Scott picks over the Twitter S-1 regulatory filing and notes weakness outside the US when it comes to ad revenues. He observes, "Put another way, Twitter had $2.58 in revenue for every 1,000 timeline views in the United States in the third quarter, compared with just 36 cents in the rest of the world, according to regulatory filings. A timeline view is when users visit their own pages that show all the tweets from people they follow." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSDVpl6p1CLVJgtR7J4g9OGUC0gkCiAeKTmlTSA_vS4hbDtnatBclETk2XdmlvwnzTjeChXPBj_rJyMzVaeAzCh7uPLNIVKRHwI2KBw-HEIkNCgrVf-VEt8tUtELnmHeG1dqYSIhwMgNrpxUITGDBHOAQs2NZq1t8pmwBwqwLfD1n6LchS30ReCcc10NJ1YCAGNjBQhvIz6yAvXUuIdEKytD> .

 

Etail Boom

 

Ecommerce companies in China are gearing up for 11/11, otherwise known as Single's Day, which is a day dedicated to online shopping, according to Ad Age. Companies produce deals and exclusive coupons, much like Cyber Monday in the US. Last year the activity caused payment system failures at some banks as the Chinese middle class cozied up to the idea of online shopping. Now, more Western companies plan to take part in the one-day sales frenzy, including Microsoft, Gap and Toys R Us. "We have an ambitious sales target, up to a month and a half's worth of sales in a single day," said Julien Chiavassa, Asia Pacific regional digital and ecommerce head for Clarins. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016o_DQWN-lSAO3UlouIa9-flthsTfA4NzGXALg7pH9OXxNTb1LTPPZ6ZpTV6Jd81-2vcxBABb_kVjlrtxWnaeL_Dqx1UQ0310_pOvvPY3iP9G8nS-wkjjgTo9r2Kgm4iLymdETMQNrz_09jbPqFf83DNwmaANqFCwqZhf5vWsXkVSZtNZB9cpA0fgGtCEgSJ3V1bOmOrYjrJZkvmSEquv700jGP6V-OcPXPqIUBiXg1I=> .

Got Your Back

 

Eric Picard's startup, Rare Crowds, had run out of money and was facing imminent shutdown, so he reached out to the 'Internet Oldtimers Group' for money and they came through for him. Ad Age got the inside story of how Internet company veterans pledged to keep Picard's firm funded and why it's back on track as a success story. "The company was not going to be able to survive without more capital," Picard told Ad Age. "Those guys stepped up and just really saved us. I mean, we were dead." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001z6Lc14xzjCQs59Qze1moFQAEZNCQS4YICyBi0PvN7T2ZSw3rmk8LnVbD-H6jhpexNS_M7zrE5wlgb76-BX77q9BQUAAuKhU5HTQyjlMVO35oPlTC6Ht3tkUYx5YW7VkeWKI0aaY_Jik5tGdCEXupXH74CvkkBTBK87oTz_ARQXNkYzQOb4L8MencmVQgK12v0tK3O7tyzMo=> .

 

Data And The Human

 

Amazon is busy perfecting its video content production capabilities, known as Amazon Studios, according to The Wall Street Journal. But Amazon's Roy Price tells the WSJ that data from reviews, for example, is only one factor in what Amazon makes or doesn't and says, "It is not the case that you walk in on Tuesday morning and the computer tells you, 'Doot doot doot, you should order these two shows." Human stuff is still required. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001z6Lc14xzjCS9vbN-P9iRqKT3tdDkLHRspAGrQXhpx5ehNX76EfPRJp-aJw4ArxUg5bsSrpeacVLalpwAM_eAedeN88D-bKCv6BU_v2WfQMww-KEkzkeBaaAchcA_zKcSnpwVWUASxsqLFE_OlXWIkIz3dtmRuJvd1Nu-L1ICFxCjC1sKgchaSqdWLoqasCylzdMkN-NHSrk=> .

 

Data Vs. Operational Tech

 

In a post on his personal blog, kbs+ Ventures' Darren Herman fields questions from the Twitterverse. A query about the race between data tech and operational efficiency tech intrigues Herman: "Up to today, I believe that data tech has captured much of the mindshare. Folks like BlueKai, Exelate, VisualIQ, Adometry, Lotame, Cross Pixel and others have nailed the data side of all of this. I don't know how they play out, but at least have captured the initial intent of the industry. For operational efficiency tech..." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001z6Lc14xzjCSt9nLUH4hbbF1d7dN4uO4zaQDJdPY_UPqYWqAoE-uxkCkQ_9qnS_Sv2UUtomBYso-U1q_9aPaoTINeD8DI6rUynH_pmcD6Vj9EH1S7lmQTN8msmqoLJeP7DWTp6Q15XgpYa1rIVSFWmc54CySfFhxedd2zyRbQEMbxq5sT5HCf9p9rWjtXpMTjbfK6f7Wxcfk12RJt_gHKfEcb0ba9EmNuoRxlfKe6Hm0=> .

 

Social Ad Limits

 

As Twitter gears up for its IPO, advertising revenue is going to garner the most investor interest, but there could be a limit to how much users are willing to tolerate, as Techcircle points out. Facebook's chief financial officer, David Ebersman, said the company is unlikely to go much higher than the current 5% ad ratio in users' news feeds. Twitter's acquisition of MoPub should help the company advertise outside the platform. Opening Up To Programmatic

 

Gawker is the latest publisher to change its mind about private exchanges as pressure to automate the ad sales process mounts. "We expect our advertising to bifurcate between the branded content produced by Studio@Gawker that we sell directly and efficient, targeted display media sold via a private exchange," said Erin Pettigrew, Gawker's business development lead. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001z6Lc14xzjCSoiryY1nJo9jxXvAeaFlQ9bQgSuTRT3TJQX_1e1UqdQ8G8Oct6Ukoki3Bj4SWhR4a-c1jdUAtEWnNwT9sGq8gnmdlr5K7KeIo-s0J8sD2ip3cd8l4IDWsH38Ixg20wanii1aU_i6-nB6cXoFj0TIGJ> .

The Merger Process Rolls On

 

The period during which US regulators could oppose the Publicis Omnicom Merger has ended without incident, according to Adweek. This means the two companies are closer to merging, which is expected to happen next year. Combined, the companies will control 40% of media buying in the US, and 20% globally. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001z6Lc14xzjCTR6PRkp9gRxDuK-_Lu9K3vmoopljliszlpYY2BWaayIR-1rGSp41auuNG7gyam1RKozm15y-YED97hX6UU2Xgr9-qpr7wCcOA3no28Thy65IGyfSnQe1UGVGKuZku-AWejjvae-CmvWF2DQJAcEM175dmXsLqtPYqSSLTFKskqoo9bIp21rc2-j_JX1jAOghuAqQchoNEH4blEOYjdyT1J> .

 

Reach Extension



In a study created with Digiday, ad network 2.0 Rocket Fuel looked at publishers' reach extension capabilities. One finding: "One in four (26%) of publishers surveyed ask higher CPMs for audience extension campaigns, as compared with their on-site inventory -- a more common practice for large publishers." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001z6Lc14xzjCRHnO6-OCGouSa1ZKJThJHB091nL3qC0x1O-ZvsUgC6n8VOuOCg40KdlhVnmHf-PpoO44s8xapvvOrGGWAb7KX5hvXvPaAqWiuLouLqjfX_QufE-Q7abymPON3W_Ix46mMmVVlyU770kB3IYWYPPrwfe7NWR5usICA=> . And download the study (Pay with some PII) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001z6Lc14xzjCTemr0GxOFa5RWB_DkjnIRP9-qUwCjRD4xpFpRlzgUqHqyFqrkkzMHDhY_HRwKbQssAno9i7yrEkx_0T0KiXH6dVVTCTPbOb1uqp0Uso4IgNkwmInjJZdm_qZ9Og6Lqc7k=> . In part, Rocket Fuel wants those direct, big publisher relationships to get in front of exchange buyers.

 

New Look For Groupon

 

Groupon has rolled a new site design that focuses heavily on search, its latest effort to keep users interested in deals, AllThingsD reported. Once a lucrative niche, deals seem to be falling out of favor with users, and Groupon has a lot to lose. According to CEO Eric Lefkofsky, the company is trying to emulate a Costco style of inventory vs. an Amazon one. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001z6Lc14xzjCSw_aCqscsI6GUfevJKfRwSkueS1xYrR-qhiG7pfECjYOus0sdTudoLc66N8C-nGBfv4B-M7tS7kBxsIPWsz21CZG2BBqMIT1yUpulQ_rya658zddFPC0E8Ko3Werk5qQuM5DwIbXtAqGqRGthxj3kGyTZtcBSuZ0nGICUigzfKLl_oT1N0kyu0zYAqBWYG4p79tt1weTWRVwV3yDP3MQa1p8cgx9ERbFA=> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QJasVv59ZlZw1GF_ksUk6sOCGoMimxOvoDwdJfId_2x7EZCce015ofqsqjGngUxkUDG9-YfcdKdxF8GSBwyMqRtIwcn8Tm97l5vUAU3VselsqNMpJmB9ANOUbTsoKeObU4s4_xzFLqc=> .

 

Ad Tech Is Back

 

Ad tech is making a comeback with investors, David Pakman points out on his blog, although it never completely went away. He notes that exchanges are currently driving a lot of ad sales and those are the companies that have investors' heads turning. Rocket Fuel and Criteo have market caps in the billions, reinforcing the idea that those in the business of selling ads are well positioned. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QJasVv59ZlYJg9E57YHDgY_T2ffflQ2b8TttYO1-hBQuCx3xRn_CMyEYHpMTru5WfktbHBlmhYXbKdGBUOFe50K6YO7CVh4aiJ6tbTc1x0dLQG56tWMRx610ZTS8om5_REOBUfg-XHCU4UNE8gPX8nvvSCyDICUSMZ2ttuROZ-G1rdb8-FNMFljycntT_MLU> .

 

Programmatic Myths

 

The term programmatic is still often misunderstood, so Digiday's Jack Marshall breaks down a few of the bigger myths to clear things up. Some of the points he makes are that RTB and programmatic are not the same thing, publishers are not "outgunned" by buyers and not everything can be bought programmatically right now. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QJasVv59ZlYfIKMbsquPmmuHovtT6hr9yR5p51R7gRzh52JfzQTcqhWROhZ7-qTSJVl_fzLJlKEXstAOPKvYt_mRg376S_KH5Qdh0b3ub_vTo7tu8FigmZki1RPOttgFd7xdB6lkQMHyzFPcAi6RWBVwaO2z5goxHn9PofSIqiE=> .

 

Leveraging Mobile Search

 

Despite not having a retail store, Lenovo noticed 20,000-30,000 mobile search queries a month for store locations. The company effectively turned Google Maps into a display ad and teamed up with local retailers that sold its products and was able to drive users to either its own site or to these stores and provided coupons as an incentive, according to Mobile Commerce Daily's Lauren Johnson. The outcome was positive for Lenovo, which plans to expand this marketing effort to all the locations where its product is available. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QJasVv59ZlawXMKMx98xcg5o2y8vu0QTXAae0A7MciCeFAWn0DiYgg4NhdFeCSDAfbFLqAZkLGRA-7rGYsmvGEK7zYItYIhLtcDQFCSSscOPlW0RDoDnEN0Wu4ea7djr0dcvt2j20149EYXZcUC1FV7l3__2HZjti33LXQdIq5Amow5u_ZBlQc8nyUS38bxK4s9VTyufdUmgj2ECDxT1Hhi1xaU9x-dRKqCIR0WehJEO9Nf9k6uMjQ==> .

 

New Relationships

 

Relationships in the online advertising world are never simple, Doug Weaver, founder and CEO of Upstream Group, points out on his blog. And they certainly aren't monogamous. In order to not get left behind in this new age of marketing relationships, companies should be more open and have a strong point of view. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QJasVv59ZlY2CiwVl_y8ZEp3eb6XYCDyndiWFS5BxG7X1kWIgxPTiqkPR3efIyhWTpYpQCk29Li3lhpL07CdkskodcVl2dcSobCmlELNexVWxzha-LVdLrrbEaBe8VLrcMMl_HCd13yX40Olo-4EwA==> .

 

Peeking In The Amazon Box...

 

...and then slamming it shut! MediaWeek's Arif Durrani gets a teeny tiny bit closer to the notoriously secretive Amazon and talks to Lisa Utzschneider, global VP of advertising sales. Although no clear answers are given, Utzschneider does say, "I want us to run ads that we're proud of. I want to see more advertising that is across screens but serves a purpose and that we all collectively raise our customer experience bar." Nice. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QJasVv59ZlYtZse3Z81OPBrOacAiUbN7sFD-PAmmrPrGta-EDRMzzosZNpPDbyvBAhGK7qAG9_Sf0gEzxHPvG9nDsIx94BDmkl4CcRrIZlV7NmBEJTCQB163BkZLUjzFAXHpBQ8GpkOhR40cRQT-BYnn0-AbyQs0tAvghic_PaonD69lvBp1KScZfZFyhmreT2bLLmMKCVO77F3ttx2GMQ==> .
